for comment 
 
Suggested changes: 
• 
Chapter 2.1 Concept model table "data model entity descriptions" clarification 
contact person relation to the description. 
• 
Chapter 3.1.2 Maintenance of customer information: details on postal and 
for the processing of business addresses and added subheadings 3.1.2.1 To the customer 
type, 3.1.2.2 Correctness and maintenance of customer data, 3.1.2.3 Encrypted 
customers and text highlights to improve findability. 
• 
Chapter 3.2.1 Addition to the paragraph Contract information about the transfer of customer data 
to all those entitled to information and reference to paragraph 3.1.2.2 and 
clarification regarding contact information 
• 
Chapter 3.2.3 Contract data changes: added clarification of contract data 
for changes that do not update the information maintained in the data hub (8) and 
automatic customer data caused by contract data updates 
for updates (9) 
29/09/2023 
preliminary 2.2 
2.2 version changes to functionality: 
• 
Added a new reason code 'Termination of the seller's activity' (AN05) for the contract 
for deciding. The seller can use the code when announcing the decision himself DH-
at the 331 event. If the operator uses the mass event for its operations 
for closing/future sales contracts of the closing seller 
to cancel sales contracts, the distribution system operator is notified 
terminations with DH-331-2 messages and cancellations with DH-341-2 messages. 
Termination messages (DH-331-2) use a new reason code 
AN05 and reason code AR02 in the cancellation messages ('Seller 
canceled the contract'). (Chapter 3.2.4) Development proposal #141 
• 
Cancellation of the customer's online contract outside the balance window will not be refunded 
agreement prior to entry into force (chapter 3.2.5.2). Development Proposal #69 
• 
If the place of use is part of the netting or energy community calculations 
under construction, the calculation does not expect measurement data for the respective usage location, but 
the calculation is performed on the measurement data of other places of use that belong to it 
by. Change regarding netting calculation in version 2.1, 
regarding the energy community calculation in version 2.2. (Chapters 3.3.7 and 3.3.8) 
Development Proposal #202 
6/7/2023 
2.1 
2.1 version changes to functionality: 
• 
Termination and cancellation of the sales contract will be notified 
to the distribution system operator also when the network contract corresponding to the sales contract 
is unconfirmed, but these do not form a process chain (Chapter 3.15). 
Development proposal #41. 
• 
The authorization cannot be notified to the distribution system operator (chapters 3.9 and 3.9.1). 
Development proposal #65. 
• 
In reasoning about the need for a new network contract, an 'electricity supply contract'-
based on the information, the existing online agreement is also taken into account (chap 
3.2.2.1). Development proposal #144. 
• 
It is also possible to update the structural information of the product 
tax rate information of the product component (chapter 3.7.3). Development proposal #9, implemented 
already to version 2.0. 
Other updates: 
• 
Updated instructions on the recommended accuracy of measurement data (chapter 3.3.1). 
Development Proposal #64. 
• 
Added a rule missing from the description, according to which the energy community 
the distribution share of an individual member's place of use cannot be 100% (chapter 3.1.4).

Changes 
• 
Refined the number of decimals allowed by the datahub in the measurement data 
in the notification and added information about the performed validation (chapter 3.3.1 and 3.3.2.2). 
• 
Added the process chain for canceling the termination of the sales contract 
to starting processes (Chapter 3.15). 
• 
Added mention of the end customer's bankruptcy situation as an example 
for retroactive termination of the contract (chapter 3.14.1). 
• 
Added a link to the instructions on datahub's control reports (chapter 2.5). 
• 
Added description usingas part of the interruption criticality of the place 
contract information to be delivered to the distribution system operator and the meaning of the information 
in a possible power shortage situation (chapter 3.2.2.1). 
• 
Refinement of the sales contract prior to the reinstatement of the previous contract 
in connection with cancellation (chapter 3.2.5.1). 
• 
Removed mention of termination of the online contract in the seller's response 
to refusing to return the contract. The distribution system operator is not here 
in the situation, come to an online agreement. Related to development proposal #121. 
(Chapter 3.2.5.2) 
• 
Added information that no more than 30 measurement data reminders are sent 
during the day (paragraph 3.3.2.4).  
• 
Removed incorrect mention of measurement area specificity of reactive electricity 
in the order for transmission of measurement data. The order cannot be placed 
per measurement area (chapter 3.3.5). 
• 
Refined/corrected descriptions of energy community calculations (chapters 3.3.8.1 and 
3.3.8.2). 
• 
Added information missing from the description of the party's own ID 
about changing to a y code in the case of a business customer (chapter 3.14.2). 
• 
Refined description of handling encrypted clients and added attention 
maintenance of customer and contract information (chapter 3.1.2). 
• 
Fixed links in document.

Definitions and abbreviations 
Time step. Information that indicates the time accuracy with which the meter registers measurement data. Finland 
the retail market is moving from hourly measurement to 15-minute measurement (quarter measurement) 
during the transition period from 1 January 2023. The time step used in the balance sheet is one hour on May 22, 2023 
until, when we move on to a 15-minute balance sheet (quarter balance). 
Regional network operator. The distribution system operator of the high-voltage distribution network, which has under its control 
high-voltage distribution network and which engages in licensed electricity network operations here 
online. 
Customer. A natural person, company, association or other entity, e.g. a municipality, which has electricity sales, 
electricity supply and/or electricity purchase agreement with the seller and/or network agreement with the distribution network operator 
with, and which acquires or produces electricity mainly for its own use. 
Open editor. A party that supplies its customer with all the electricity it needs or 
balances the difference between the production and purchase of the customer's electricity and the use and delivery 
by supplying the missing amount of electricity or receiving the surplus during each hour (Here 
in connection with this, the customer can also mean operators, deviating from what is defined above). 
CET time. Central European time zone (Central European Time). 
Datahub (datahub system). A centralized information exchange solution for the electricity retail market, 
whose operation is described in this document. 
Datahub event. An event where the datahub receives and processes the party 
sent message and forward messages to other parties. 
Data standard. Separately published Excel formatnen data table, which contains the exact data hub 
attribute- and relation-specific definitions. 
ebIX. European forum for energy Business Information eXchange. A European organization that 
develop information exchange in the energy sector. 
Previous seller. An electricity seller whose sales contract has ended at the place of use of a new seller 
as a result of the new sales agreement announced. 
eSet. Balance clearing unit. Jointly owned by Fingrid, Statnett and Svenska Kraftnät 
a service company that is responsible for the operational activities of the joint Nordic balance sheet settlement model. 
ET. Energiateollisuus ry is a business political association representing the electricity and district heating sector 
labor market political interest organization. 
Fingrid Datahub Oy. The entirety of Fingrid Oyj, established for Datahub's operational activities 
owned subsidiary. The short form Datahub can also be used below.

GLN (Global Location Number). GS1 system identifier used to identify the party 
in datahub. The GLN identifier is a 13-character identifier consisting of a GS1 company identifier, 
of freely selectable numbers (3-5 pcs) and a check number. 
GS1. An international organization that distributes unique organization-specific identifiers. Finland 
the country code is 64. The country code and the one connected to it are issued by GS1 Finland Oy's customer service 
the company-specific identifier is collectively known as the GS1 company identifier (GS1 Company Prefix). 
The company identifier can be used to create other identifiers, such as GLN and GSRN identifiers. 
GSRN (Global Service Relation Number). GS1 system identifier used to identify 
measurement point in the data hub. The GSRN identifier consists of a GS1 company identifier, a serial number and 
from the check number.. 
Price time series. Determines the price of a specific product component for each regular interval 
(for example for each lesson) 
Main. An electrical network with a nominal voltage lower than 110 kilovolts. 
Distribution system operator. A network operator that controls a distribution network or high-voltage lines 
distribution network and which engages in licensed electricity network operations in this network. E-commerce 
within the scope of the centralized information exchange balance sheet are the distribution system operators who practice 
electricity network operation in the distribution network referred to in the Electricity Market Act and which have been granted 
electricity network license for electricity network operation in a distribution network or a closed distribution network. 
The distribution network means an electrical network with a nominal voltage lower than 110 kilovolts. 
Distribution network balance sheet. Balance statement of the measurement area or areas of the distribution network as it is 
defined in the Electricity Market Act and the Electricity Market Regulations. 
Calendar time series. Defines the times when a certain product component (such as daily or 
night electricity) price is valid. 
Network operator. System-responsible network operator (Fingrid Oyj). 
Consumer. Consumer referred to in Chapter 1 § 4 of the Consumer Protection Act (38/1978). The consumer is 
a natural person who acquires electricity mainly for a purpose other than his business 
for business activities. 
Place of use. A concept related to a physical location, for example an apartment, that connects the customer 
through the network and sales agreement to the distribution network operator and the electricity seller and where the electricity 
consumption or production can be measured.. In Datahub, the place of use is a logical point (logical point of 
delivery). 
Business process. A set of related tasks that are done to achieve a defined goal, 
for example, in order to achieve a customer's change of seller 
Reading (or measurement reading). Cumulative reading registered by the measuring equipment.

Reading measurement. A measurement that registers cumulative readings. . 
Pass-through billing. A procedure where the seller or the distribution system operator invoices the other party for their own 
its services, which this party continues to bill the customer for. 
Market balance area. A geographical area for which the electricity market determines a common price 
for each moment in time (i.e. price time series). The market balance area consists of measurement areas. 
(Market) process. A business process between market participants that involves the parties 
exchange of information between Processes include contract processes, such as moves and vendor changes, and 
delivery of measurement data and balance settlement. 
Market participant or electricity market participant. In the electricity retail market together or 
a company operating in several rolestys or party. Parties to the electricity retail market include, among others 
e.g. distribution system operators, electricity sellers, balance managers, balance clearing unit and third parties 
the parties. The party must have an agreement with Datahub. 
Meter. A device or combination of devices that registers the consumption or production of electricity. Meter 
may also contain an integrated or separate control device that can be used to control the place of use 
electrical devices or, for example, other meters of an apartment building. 
Timestamp of the measurement. Information related to the measurement, which tells the moment in time for which the energy was measured 
to be registered. 
Measurement (time series). A concept that refers to a certain measurement point (place of use, limit point or 
production unit) related measurement data and related metadata, such as the time series identifier. 
Measurement time series are time series whose measurement data is based on a business basis 
to the information registered by electricity meters, usually electricity consumption or production. 
Measurement time series are also called measurements in abbreviated form.  
Measurement range. The measurement area refers to the main grid, high-voltage distribution grid, 
distribution network, closed distribution network or part thereof or real estate or the like 
the property group's internal electricity network, which forms its own settlement area in the balance sheet. 
The measurement area is delimited from the other measurement areas of the boundary point measurement. 
Measurement setting. Decree of the Government on electricity supplies established on the basis of the Electricity Market Act 
survey and measurement. 
Measurement point. A point where electricity consumption, production or transmission can be determined. The specification can 
happen by measuring, based on an estimate or by calculation. The measuring point can be a place of use, 
border point or production unit. 
Measurement register. A logical or physical entity contained in a meter that registers a certain 
measurement object, such as active power input to the network or reactive power taken from the network. The registry might 
contains hourly data or cumulative readings of reading measurement.

For the area he applied for a closed distribution network permit from the Energy Agency. If the area is processed

party responsible for measurement. The owner of the closed distribution network is subject to the same data delivery responsibility 
rules than the distribution network operator. 
High-voltage distribution network. Local or regional with a nominal voltage of 110 kilovolts 
an electric network or cable that is not a connection cable and that does not cross the national border.

1 
Introduction 
1.1 
To the reader 
During 2014, Fingrid carried out a survey related to the electricity retail market 
about the future solution of information exchange. The report ended up recommending the establishment of a data hub 
To Finland. The Ministry of Labor and the Economy processed the report during the spring and on April 8, 2015 
in a letter, the ministry asked Fingrid to initiate an investigationthe implementation of the centralised 
data exchange solution described in the document. 
Datahub's business processes and its technical interface description have been defined in close cooperation with the 
industry in autumn 2015. The description of the processes has been supported by working groups appointed by the Finnish Energy Industries 
composed of representatives of the industry. The document, Business processes of the electricity retail market in Datahub, was submitted to the entire industry for comment and, based on the review of the comments, the first official version of the document was published on 
March 21, 2016. 
Close cooperation with the industry has been a basic requirement for the success of the definition work and a 
cost-effective approach. The members of the working groups have also served as an important 
link between the process work and the industry, bringing a broad view and 
expertise of the industry to the work. 
As the Datahub project progresses, a process working group composed of representatives of vendors and distribution network operators will support the project. The task of the process working group is to support the datahub project in handling the needs for and proposals for changes to the datahub 
business processes and data exchange definition documents efficiently, fairly and taking into account any potential 
multiple impacts on the sector. You can read more about the working group's activities on the datahub 
service portal, where all the project working groups are described. 
1.2 
Legislation concerning the operation of Datahub 
In accordance with the current Electricity Market Act, the task of the transmission system operator with system responsibility, i.e. 
Fingrid Oyj, is to develop the information exchange required for electricity trading and balance settlement in its area of ​​responsibility in cooperation with electricity companies. 
In addition to the above, Fingrid Oyj is responsible for the centralized organization of the information exchange and management required for the electricity trading 
market processes in the distribution networks, as well as for balance settlement in the distribution networks in its area of ​​responsibility. The centralised information exchange services for electricity trading 
(Datahub services described in section 1.2.1) are clearly listed and defined in the Electricity Market Act. 
The operational activities of the centralised information exchange services for electricity trading will be handled by Fingrid 
Oyj's wholly owned subsidiary Fingrid Datahub Oy. 
In order to make the interpretation of the law and its connection to the defined business processes clearer, the 
Datahub services, responsibilities and obligations of the various parties defined by the law, as well as the

1.2.1 
Datahub services 
The Electricity Market Act defines Datahub's tasks, i.e. the services it provides. The services in question 
refer to the business processes described in this document. 
Datahub services defined in the law are: 
1. maintenance of customer data and electricity consumption point data of retailers and distribution system operators; 
2. organisation of the exchange of information required by customer contract processes in retail sales and electricity distribution; 
3. organising the exchange of measurement data that forms the basis for billing and balance settlement; 
4. organising the exchange of data on electricity supplies and electricity distribution disconnection and connection processes; 
5. organising the maintenance of the distribution system operator's product and invoice line data and the possibility of maintaining the retailer's product and invoice line data; 
6. transmitting the retailer's and the distribution system operator's party information; 
7. access by the retailer's and the distribution system operator's customers to their own data held by the centralised electricity trade information exchange unit; 
8. organising the balance settlement of electricity trades in distribution networks and the exchange of data related to balance settlement; 
9. storing the data covered by the services referred to in paragraphs 1–8. 
1.2.2 
Data stored in Datahub and its disclosure 
As mentioned in the previous paragraph, the storage of data stored in Datahub is one of 
Datahub's services. The definitions of business processes take into account the legal requirements related to data protection 
and therefore only the data required for business processes is stored in Datahub. Section 2.3 of this document describes in more detail how long data is stored and how the data is deleted after this storage period. 
Datahub will not disclose information other than on the basis of contractual rights or authorization given by the customer. Authorizations are described in section 3.8. 
More information about data protection in general is provided in section 1.5. 
1.2.3 
Parties using Datahub 
The Electricity Market Act clearly defines which electricity market parties are 
obliged to use Datahub services in the electricity retail marketnot in information exchange.  
A retailer and a distribution system operator who conducts electricity network operations in the distribution network must 
use datahub's services in the exchange of information on the electricity retail market. With a distribution network 
refers to an electrical network with a nominal voltage lower than 110 kilovolts (the nominal voltage is 
specified in the electricity network permit). Distribution system operator means a system operator that has

who have been granted an electricity grid license for electricity grid operations in a distribution network or in a closed one 
in the distribution network (nominal voltage lower than 110 kV). What these networks have in common is that they have 
places of use of the distribution network, with which it is necessary to organize related electricity market processes 
in accordance with uniform procedures. 
On the other hand, the obligation to use datahub's services does not apply to the distribution network operators who operate 
high-voltage distribution network or similar closed distribution network, i.e. these distribution system operators 
are not covered by datahub's services. Neither do the holders of these measuring areas who do not have 
electricity network license (e.g. industrial networks and production networks in the balance sheet) are not datahub's 
within the scope of the service. 
1.2.4 
Responsibilities and obligations of the parties 
The Electricity Market Act describes both datahub and the parties using datahub's services 
responsibilities and obligations.  
As explained in the previous paragraph, a retailer and a distribution system operator who engages 
electricity network operations in the distribution network, you must use the data hub's services for electricity 
in the exchange of information in the retail market. Essential from the point of view of datahub's business processes 
is that the parties are also responsible for the correctness of the information they provide to datahub and 
for correcting any errors without delay. Datahub does not make the information to be delivered 
checks for correctness, but checks that the information to be submitted contains everything 
mandatory information for the process and that the information to be submitted is in the correct format. 
The parties must also ensure that their information systems and those used for data transfer 
their systems are compatible with datahub.  
Datahub's responsibility is to organize the previously mentioned services and related retailers and 
storage of data provided by distribution system operators and services provided by the data hub 
that is, organizing the information exchange of the business processes described in this document. Part 
with the use of the data hub, the responsibilities of the distribution network operators are transferred to the scope of the data hub's responsibilities, such as 
for example, making a distribution system operator's balance sheet. 
One of the responsibilities transferred from the distribution system operator to the data hub is the reporting of electricity consumption data 
for the end user of electricity. Datahub will offer customers the opportunity to view their own 
their information in the customer portal implemented for this purpose. This has been explained in more detail 
in chapter 3.12.

regulation (VNA) on the investigation and measurement of electricity supplies, which details the parties 
duties and obligations regarding electricity supplies and balance sheet settlement. Both Work and

1.3 
Development in retail market data exchange datahub 
with 
The most important improvements and changes to the current one offered by datahub are presented below 
for information exchange. 
Centralized synchronous data exchange 
With Datahub, from party to party based on data transmission operators 
from information exchange to centralized information exchange. In the future, all information will be reported to datahub, 
where the information is processed and forwarded to other actors entitled to the information. The most significant difference 
the current practice is that all information exchange goes through one point, where everything 
the improvements described in this chapter to the current operation can be made possiblea. 
One of the most significant developments brought about by the data hub is the transition from the current main 
from batch-based asynchronous data exchange to synchronous data exchange. 
In practice, this means that datahub responds to the party's notifications immediately. In the future 
for example, after notifying the sales contract, the seller does not have to wait for the distribution system operator 
confirmation, but information about the acceptance or rejection of the contract is returned to the seller 
in real time directly from the data hub. This feature together with carefully designed processes 
with will reduce the need for clarification between the parties. Possible problems with new ones 
contracts can be processed with the customer immediately during the same customer contact. 
Unified customers for online and sales contracts 
Nowadays, customers of online and sales contracts often differ from each other. Online contract can 
for example, to be owned by the husband and the sales contract may be shared by the couple. However, there is in the field 
had a strong common vision that these contracts should have the same customers and different ones 
to avoid problem situations. 
In practice, achieving this goal requires uniform contractual practices. In the future 
the distribution system operator receives a notification from the data hub about the sales contract concluded for the point of use and 
of the customers connected here. If necessary, Datahub creates a network contract for the place of use 
for customers corresponding to the sales contract to be confirmed by the distribution system operator in the data hub. Bridge 
the operating method ensures that the online and sales contracts will always be the same in the future 
to customers.  
The method of operation is the valid procedure guidelines of the current Energiateollisuus ry 
according to, i.e. the customer should always be directed to contact the seller in the first place. This 
the operating method also requires that new contracts must always be drawn up for those with legal capacity 
to customers. The distribution system operator cannot be required to act contrary to this principle. For new ones

Y-IDs of companies and personal IDs of consumer customers must always be indicated on contracts. 
An exception is allowed only in situations where the person does not have a Finnish personal identification number. 
Transfer of the distribution system operator's balance sheet to the data hub 
With the introduction of Datahub, currently the distribution system operator's calculations and balance sheet 
the reported sum deliveries per seller and the distribution system operator's losses are calculated in the data hub. 
Datahub also calculates vendor-specific balance error corrections and informs the distribution network operator 
vendor-specific balance sheet errors for invoicing vendors. With Datahub, the distribution network operator does not 
need to perform the calculations described above in their own system and do not maintain information 
of the sellers of the place of use for balance settlement calculations. Datahub will deliver the necessary 
balance sheet information for eSett and for the retail market, the market parties are in contact 
Instead of eSett's system, to datahub in matters related to the balance sheet of the distribution network. 
Sellers and distribution system operators can monitor their own through the interface provided by datahub 
balance settlement information, including amount delivery information and balance error information. Datahub too 
reports to the distribution system operators about places of use without vendors, so that the distribution system operator knows 
to cut off the electricity in places of use without vendors. 
Intensification of supervision 
In the current exchange of information, there are situations where the market parties do not work together 
in accordance with the agreed game rules. Monitoring tools will be created in Datahub, with the help of which 
the activities of operators can be monitored. The purpose of monitoring is to collect material with which possible 
abuses and deviations from the common rules of the game can be pointed out and wronged 
with this, the activity can be intervened. 
Information exchange of product and billing information 
Current message traffic does not exchange product or billing information related to the place of use. Datahub 
enables the maintenance and exchange of information on sales and transfer products. With this 
the market participants can, if they wish, take into account the other party, i.e. the seller or 
the distribution system operator, the product chosen for the place of use in its own product selection, and thus offer 
uniform products for the customer both in terms of transmission and electricity sales. 
Datahub also enables the transmission of invoice lines. Market participants can report if they wish 
invoice lines to the data hub, from where they are delivered to the seller of the point of use, the distribution system operator or 
to an authorized 3rd party in the counter lines. This makes it easier for different people 
utilization of invoicing service providers in business and one online service and 
including energy salesrather than offering the invoice to the customer. 
Utilization of service providers 
Datahub will make it easier for market parties to utilize various service providers 
in business. Standardized interfaces and a centralized data exchange solution reduce 
data exchange costs, when service providers, i.e. so-called 3rd parties, do not have to 
organizes data transfer connections with each market party separately.

Comprehensive and high-quality information content 
In connection with defining the Datahub processes, all market participants were surveyed 
information needed in business, which should be exchanged between sellers, distribution system operators and 3rd parties 
between. This means an expansion of the information content to be exchanged compared to the current information exchange. 
In the information on the place of use, for example, information about the place of use will be available in the future 
about the possibility of remote connection. 
In Datahub, the quality of information will also be better than at present. Datahub has validations and 
control, which can be used to prevent the storage and transmission of incomplete and technically incorrect information. 
The most significant improvements concern the use of customers' unique identifiers (personal identification numbers and Y-
identifiers) maintenance, measurement data and address data.  
Measurement data based on continuous measurement 
In Finland, there has been a transition to comprehensive hourly measurement and the remaining traditional so-called 
the number of reading measurements is constantly decreasing. Datahub's functionalities are defined in such a way that 
the special treatment of the reading measurements is taken into account only in the most necessary parts.  
With Datahub, transmission of cumulative readings is not supported in data exchange. The distribution system operator 
should be made up of reading measurements and unmeasured items Specific to the place of use 
hourly time series for balance settlement and information transmission. It should be noted that the datahub 
with the implementation, a separate smoothing calculation of the measured reading data will not be performed.  
Datahub will also support a 15-minute balance settlement cycle that is more frequent than an hour. 
Supporting statutory reporting 
Comprehensive information related to the place of use, the customer and contracts is brought to Datahub. This 
the information content can be used in creating statutory reports for operators. 
Services for 3rd parties 
Datahub facilitates the business of various service providers. Customer, seller or 
authorized by the distribution system operator, a third party has the opportunity to use the 
and customer-specific information including measurement data from one place. Ad hoc 
3. the parties must enter into an agreement with datahub, which obligates the party to the common 
to comply with the rules of the game. 
A more customer-oriented service 
All the development described above aims to make business more efficient and more customer-oriented 
to the service. Datahub's contract processes reduce error and problem situations that arise 
as a better service for the customer. The services described above for 3rd parties will also be added 
offering various customer services. The principle is that the data hub works as a joint industry 
as a back-end system that enables companies in the industry to offer their customers 
better customer service.

Business development 
Datahub will also play a significant role in the development of various business operations. In public 
in the discussion, different visions of future electricity are brought up more and more often 
from the retail market. The key themes in this discussion are consumer demand elasticity, 
electric car charging and various energy efficiency and management services. Datahub is coming 
to enable and contribute to various new services and what they need 
development of information exchange. 
1.4 
Business in a datahub environment 
The parties work in the data hub with different roles. The roles are divided at the top level to reflect that 
role model, which is used in EDIEL-based information exchange. With the introduction of Datahub 
these roles used in the current data exchange will be shared in the system 
to a more precise process level, in accordance with the information exchange processes, based on the ebIX role model. 
ebIX is a European cooperation platform for the development of information exchange in the energy industry. This one 
with the role model, the aim is to create a common terminology and through this to facilitate e.g. 
systems development. The role model in questionia has also been used in the data hubs of other Nordic countries
in projects, so bringing it to the Finnish retail market also supports the Nordic countries 
harmonization of the electricity market.  
The ebIX role model identifies all the roles that can be used in the electricity market in Europe. 
The model covers both wholesale and retail markets, but Datahub does not have one 
appropriate to implement all ebIX roles, but only where applicable 
to support defined market processes. The roles according to the ebIX model are by nature 
logical ones, such as the balance sheet manager. More detailed descriptions of the ebIX role model can be found at ebIX 
from the website https://www.ebix.org/artikel/role_model.  
A more detailed breakdown of the roles of the parties in the data hub allows, for example, access rights 
according to a specific set of needs. Rights can be linked to a specific role model 
access to information or rights to perform certain processes or events. 
Current developments seem to change the operation of market participants in a direction where 
market participants widely use their partner networks and their own service providers 
to carry out its activities. Datahub will support this trend by enabling it 
the use of more precise roles and thereby facilitate the assignments of market participants 
giving to service providers for a certain pre-defined task.  For example 
the distribution network operator can give the measurement information to the company providing the commissioned measurement services 
to datahub for delivery. In this case, the assignment is given to a specific service provider 
for the role according to which access rights, rights to send the event and 
rights to datahub information needed in the event.  
In the following chapters, it is summarized by role how datahub will change operators 
daily business.

1.4.1 
Sellers 
The main tasks of salespeople in the data hub are the initiation of contract processes and customer information 
maintenance. Contract processes include notification of new contracts, customer moves and 
in connection with changes of the seller, changes to contracts during delivery and contracts 
terminations. 
Datahub enables an even more customer-oriented and customer-friendly service for sellers. Seller 
get the necessary amount of information about the basic information of the location of use to enter into a sales contract. 
In addition, the seller can, with the authorization given by the customer, check the valid place of use, 
web product1-, and measurement information before the actual contract is concluded, if applicable 
necessary. If necessary, the seller can, before announcing the contract, by the customer 
with the authorization also checks whether the customer has a valid license preventing the conclusion of the contract 
a sales contract for a place of use that is temporary or contains unusual terms of termination. The seller does not 
however, with an authorization, you can get more detailed information about a place of use for which the customer has 
there is no contract yet. This means, for example, the place of use where the customer is moving. 
The seller can also check the connection status of the point of use and inform about possible connection fees 
for the customer in quick moving situations. A more real-time exchange of information will reduce the variety 
problems and their investigation, which improves the customer's service experience.  
Nowadays, challenges are also created by the fact that the seller must determine whether it is a move or the seller 
exchange. Notifications sent with the wrong reason code always require manual processing. In the future 
the seller does not need to do this reasoning, because datahub always has information about the place of use 
about the customer's situation and datahub returns a notice to the seller of the reason for the creation of the contract 
in the receipt. 
In the ebIX role model, the seller has no other role than Balance Supplier, i.e. the Seller who is responsible 
about the electricity contract with the customer and the sale of electricity within the contract or, if applicable 
is from the small production location, the purchase of electricity.   
1.4.2 
Distribution system operators 
In Datahub, the distribution network operator's main tasks are to maintain the usage location, network contract and 
product information of online contracts and maintain the structural information needed for the balance sheet, 
such as border points and production units (Production Unit). In addition to the above, the distribution system operator must 
reports the measurement data daily to the data hub, from where it is forwarded to the parties entitled to the information. 
Although measurement data statuses and their use are also validated in the data hub, there is measurement data 
correctness is still the responsibility of the distribution system operator. Therefore, the distribution system operator must perform its own 
validation of measurement data in the future. 
With the change brought by Datahub, the distribution network managertija can waive its own balance sheet settlement, balance sheet error
/for their compensation and loss calculations. The invoicing of balance errors is still carried out by the distribution system operator 
by, even if the calculation is performed in the data hub. With the introduction of Datahub

equivalent. In this case, the service provider can deliver the measurement data to the data hub of the distribution system operator 
on behalf of. However, the distribution system operator remains responsible for the information provided.  
1.4.3 
Customers 
From the customers' point of view, the datahub will mainly be in the electricity retail market 
the background system used by the parties, the use of which is not visible to the customer when he deals with electricity 
with the seller or distribution network operator. Datahub and renewed market processes 
the implementation is seen by customers as better and faster customer service 
during the processing times of contractual transactions. Datahub enables the customer to be more active than at present 
role as a consumer and also a producer of electricity. In particular, easier access to information by 3rd parties 
based on the customer's authorizations, will increase the various services offered to customers 
quantity. Datahub enables a more comprehensive coverage of the customer's own electricity usage 
providing services and an overall view to the customer, even in situations where the customer has multiple 
the places of use are sold by different sellers or in the measurement area of ​​different distribution system operators. 
The customer will have the opportunity to check their own data stored in the data hub for them 
through a targeted customer portal. The customer's login to the service will be implemented 
Through the national Suomi,fi service maintained by the Population Register Center. Powered by Datahub 
the service will cover the current distribution system operator's statutory reporting obligation to its own 
to their customers. From the service in question, the customer can add and remove authorizations given to the parties 
to their own information. In accordance with the Electricity Market Act and the valid data protection regulation, consumer

1.4.4 
3. Parties 
Previously describedin accordance with datahub will facilitate the business of 3rd parties with information 
due to better availability. Datahub will require a service contract from 3rd parties 
signing. The service contract specifies what kind of service the party can access data for 
use and other conditions for using the service. The 3rd party always acts as authorized by the customer or the seller 
or commissioned by the distribution system operator. Authorizations are described in more detail in this document 
in chapter 3.9.  
In general, the 3rd party can be any party registered in datahub with a contract 
with the datahub operator. A seller or 
a distribution network operator who does not have the right to the customer's data within the scope of the contract. 
As mentioned earlier, the distribution system operator can give an order for the delivery of measurement data 
datahub to a 3rd party, in which case the service provider acts as a collector of measurement data. 3rd party 
can also provide a service directly to the customer, in which case it acts as an Energy Service Company, i.e 
Energy service provider. In such a role, the 3rd party must be authorized by the customer 
to the customer's information. The 3rd party can also act in the role of Billing Agent, which is loosely translated 
A process service provider, in which case it works either on behalf of the seller or the distribution system operator. 
In this case, the seller or the distribution network operator can forward, for example, invoice line data to a 3rd party who handles it 
customer billing for this. The term Process service provider describes better here 
the party acting in the role, because this can provide other services to the parties than 
billing service.  
1.4.5 
Datahub operator 
With the data hub, a new party is born in the electricity retail market. Datahub operator 
the primary task is to maintain the datahub system and provide technical support for operators 
for main users. Other tasks include, for example, general guidance related to the industry's data hub, 
Supervision of compliance with the terms of Datahub's service contracts and the agreed game rules, various 
investigation of error situations requested by market parties and the development of the data hub and information exchange 
in close cooperation with the industry. 
In the ebIX model, the data hub operator does not have a direct role in data exchange. 
When the balance settlement of the distribution network moves to the data hub, the role related to the balance settlement ebIX-
in the Metered Data Aggregator model to be handled by the datahub.

1.5 
Data protection 
An essential part of the management of customer and location data is the datahub's registered users 
data protection, which means the protection of people's private lives. Datahub and market processes 
the design is made from the premise that all information that can be connected to the customer is 
personal information. Such information is personal information regardless of whether this information can be linked 
to a single person in the data hub. For example, the address of the place of use is independent of personal information 
whether the person's name or social security number is stored in the datahub. Place of use for personal information 
what makes an address is that the customer's address is generally relatively easy to find out. This 
also applies to situations where the customer does not live at the specific address of the place of use. 
The market processes are designed in such a way that the data hub is only saved in market processes 
the necessary information and the parties can apply for or can be forwarded information from the datahub only to them 
according to predetermined rights. These rights depend on the party's role, 
about the contractual situation and existing authorizations.

1.7 
Contents of this document 
Chapter 2 describes the requirements of the market processes for the data hub's internal data model, as well as 
descriptions of the main data groups. The chapter also describes the rights of each datahub party 
to information.  
Chapter 3 describes the business processes and operating models of the electricity retail market, which 
datahub supports. This description contains the principles and rules for how parties apply and report 
information to the data hub, and how information is transmitted to other parties as part of market processes. Description 
contains descriptions of overall processes from the business perspective of the parties. More specific 
event-specific descriptions are described in the Datahub events document, which has been published 
also in datahub's service portal.  
1.8 
Reading instructions for UML descriptions 
In this document, flowcharts (in UML 
activity diagram). The costs of market processes are presented as sequence diagrams and 
the data contents of the notifications and other descriptions of the data models are described with class diagrams. 
When interpreting the document, remember that although the UML notation is largely standardized, this is not 
however, do not mean that UML models are completely free of interpretation. Large entities 
can always be modeled from different perspectives and UML is generally used for many different ones 
for uses (e.g. software development vs. business processes) that require different 
interpretation. Especially a single diagram can at best only show a part of the background 
of the whole. There are also a lot of alternative ways of presenting something and even forced interpretation 
always reserve ice. In this document, no attempt has been made to be as orthodox as possible 
From the point of view of UML's technical specification, but to create as illustrative and easy as possible 
comprehensible presentations.  
To create the diagrams and modeling of the electricity retail market in this document, there is 
used MagicDraw software (No Magic, Inc.), which is the same as NordREG 
the software used in the harmonization project and ebIX. Below is a brief introduction to UML diagrams 
for interpretation. More UML information can be found on the Internet, especially in English. This document 
for example, Wikipedia2 and http://www.uml-diagrams.org -
website. More information and a link to the official UML documentation can also be found 
From the UML website of the Object Management Group, which manages the development of UML3.

TABLE 111 UML CONNECTION TYPES USED IN THIS DOCUMENT 
Connection type 
Definition 
 
Generalization:the object at the tip is a generalization of the source at the other end. 

Association: a connection between objects that has a counterpart in reality. 
A possible arrow at the end of the line indicates in this document in which 
direction the connection name (e.g. "contains") is read. 

Strong composition: the entity at the unchecked end is essentially 
part of the entity at the checked end. For example, customer data is an integral part of a 
contract. 

Dependency: The source is somehow dependent on the object. This 
type of connection is always used in this document with a qualifying text or 
stereotype. 
1.8.2 
Class diagrams 
Class diagrams consist of so-called entities, the relationships between them, and the 
data contained in the entities. An entity represents a specific physical or logical (data) entity. Examples of 
entities are a point of use and a sales contract. The image below shows an example of 
entities that occur in message traffic. 
• 
The entity names are written in bold at the top of the box describing the entity. 
• 
Below the line below the name are the entity attributes, or data fields. The square brackets 
following the attributes define the multiplicity of the attribute, or information about how 
many values ​​the data field can or should contain. For example, [0..1] means that the field is 
optional (or only mandatory in certain situations) and [1] means that the value is mandatory. 
If there can be an unspecified number of values, the * character is used for this purpose. 
A similar notation is also used to describe connections between entities. As shown in the 
image below, for example, there may not be a sales contract for a point of use. 
This is indicated by writing 0..1 at the end of the sales contract of the connection between these two entities. If no value is written separately for 
diversity at the end of the connection, the diversity is 1 by default.

1.8.3 
Sequence diagrams 
Sequence diagrams show the flow of a process and in particular the exchange of information between actors. 
The different roles of the process are placed on the horizontal axis and time is shown on the vertical axis. In this document, 
each exchange of information between roles is numbered. As a rule, messages occur in numerical order over time. However, this can be deviated from by using subsequences. The alt, par, opt and loop subsequences used in this 
document are explained below. 
• 
in the graphs, the time limits within {} brackets are days, unless otherwise specified in the graph; 
• 
in the {} brackets, the notation is {earliest..latest} 
NOTE! it is also possible that only one of these time limits is specified. If 
no earliest or latest limit is specified, there is no corresponding binding time limit; 
• 
in the time limits, negative numbers mean the time before the start of delivery and the entry into force of the 
contract amendment or other change, and positive numbers mean the time 
after these.

www.fingrid.fi 

The optional flow of a process is described by the opt (option) subsequence. In the example above, 
party 1 always sends message 1 to party 2, but party 2 only sends message 2 if [condition] 
is met.

can be sent in parallel or in either order. However, this does not mean that 
neither of the messages can be left unsent. 
Loop 
A loop subsequence is repeated as many times as a certain condition written in square brackets 
is valid. An example of a loop is shown in the figure below.

Datahub's data model and the parties' rights to

2.1 
Description of the conceptual model 
This section describes Datahub's internal data model at a conceptual level, i.e. the structure in which 
the data submitted by the parties to Datahub and generated by Datahub is stored. The data model does not describe 
the datahub's physical database, and is not a complete description of the future Datahub data model, but 
it describes the most important data sets for market processes and their relationships to each other. 
The attributes of the main data groups are listed in the data model images attached to Chapter 3 of this document. 
A more detailed definition of each attribute can be found in a separately published Excel data table (so-called 
data standard). When reading the images, it should be noted that information marked as optional in the image may be mandatory depending on other information. For example, the fuse size of the point of use is 
mandatory if the electrical power of the point of use has not been reported. 
The contents of the information sent by the parties to Datahub in processes and transmitted by Datahub to the parties in processes are described in the event-specific class diagrams in sections 4-12 of the Datahub Events document.

2.3 
Data retention period 
Information is stored in the data hub according to the needs of the parties' processes. Information cannot 
however, stored in the datahub forever. Storage time of measurement data in the operational data hub 
there are six years in the database, and this time also guides other processes 
storage of redundant data. When the customer's contract ends, the customer and 
contract information from datahub's operational database after the same six-year period, 
when the last measurement data related to the customer is deleted. Contract information is calculated 
in addition to the actual contract information, also invoice line information related to the contract to be deleted and 
customer data includes all data directly connected to the customer, such as the customer's authorization data. Also 
places of use in disabled status are deleted if there is not a single contract associated with them. 
The picture below shows the process by which datahub will delete the history data above 
according to the described procedure.

2.4 
User interface of the parties 
Datahub offers a browser-based user interface for use by all market participants, where 
the parties can manage their own party information, assignments between the parties and 
settings related to the use of datahub's message interface. In the user interface, the parties can also 
view all data hub data related to market processes to which the party has access 
in accordance with paragraph 2.2, the right.  
The user interface of Datahub's parties has two different types of user groups. Another group of users 
consists of parties that use in the exchange of information related to market processes 
as a rule, a message interface from their own system. As a rule, these users do not 
maintain the information related to market processes in the user interface for processingis specified 
processing processes based on the message interface. This information needs to be updated 
through the message interface, so that the data is consistent between the operators' systems and the data hub 
can be verified. In this case, market processes are mainly managed through the user interface 
e.g. structural information related to the balance sheet and information for which it has not been deemed necessary 
determine market messages, as well as some less common market processes such as 
previous seller's approval for a change of seller in retroactive error correction situations. These 
special market processes are described separately in chapter 3. As a rule, such an interface 
it is possible for the main user of the using party to give one to his own system user 
user role with which these processes can be maintained directly in the datahub user interface. 
However, the party must then ensure that the same information reported to the data hub can be saved 
to the party's own system in such a way that no new notification is sent to datahub. I.e 
the party is then responsible for the compatibility of data between the data hub and the party's own system 
by himself.  
Another group of users using the user interface consists of market participants who do not either 
due to low process execution times or some other reason, it is not profitable to build 
message interface for information exchange of market processes. These market participants are offered 
possibility to manually perform all data processing of market processes 
in the user interface. The same applies to market processes performed via the user interface

rules and checks of the correctness of data than the actual ones carried out through interfaces 
message processes. It should be noted, however, that this possibility is not suitable for large 
for processing data volumes. Because of this, there is no notification of measurement data or calculation line data 
possible through the party's user interface. Measurement, balance sheet and 
invoice line information is also not forwarded to the party's user interface separately in message form.

transmission of information to himself from the System via the message interface. 
Search events can be used both via the message interface and directly from the user interface. 
For example, measurement data can be retrieved both via the interface and the user interface. 
The measurement data retrieved from the user interface is returned as a control report in .csv format.  
The management of the parties' users is based on a model where the parties have one or more main users, 
who can grant access rights to other users of their own organization. Users can 
set the rights to both view and edit the data, or only view. Datahub 
also enables access rights to be defined in such a way that only certain users of the organization have them 
there is an opportunity to see personal data. User management instructions can be found in datahub 
from the service portal.  
Through the user interface of the parties, the parties can check the information between the parties 
assignments and maintains authorizations between the parties. Assignments and parties 
authorizations are described in chapter 3.9.2 of this document. 
Datahub offers the parties standard reports in the user interface by the parties themselves 
for review. Some of the reports correspond to what the operator needs in his own operations 
for all parties, but the parties see these reports as relevant to themselves 
information. The reports are produced using the Power-BI tool.

2.5 
Information interface for market participants 
Data exchange through the data hub is handled as described in the Datahub transactions document 
with message traffic based on ebIX message specifications. The parties will have 
also use the user interface intended for them, which is described in chapter 2.4 of this document. 
In addition to these, datahub will also offer the parties a so-called data interface, which 
with the help of this, the parties can be more flexibly offered information that belongs to them directly without events 
related messages. The data interface is implemented as a REST/HTTP interface. The data interface makes it possible 
e.g. searching for data in the datahub directly for the market party's end customers 
to the online service provided. Data cannot be reported to datahub via the data interface. 
Market participants can decide themselves whether they want to use this interface in their own 
in its operation. If the parties need to search for a larger amount of data at once, for example 
to compare the information in the data hub with the information in their own system, comes to this purpose 
use control reports provided by datahub. These reports can be run on a schedule, e.g. 
at night without disturbing other daily activities. 
The data interface can also be used when an external registered party (3rd party or other 
market participant) develops and creates new services for which the customer can authorize their own 
to their information. 3rd party service can be e.g. an application with which the end user can see his own data 
regardless of all their places of use, in which network area they are located or who sells to them 
electricity.  
From the data interface, information can be queried for a single record (customer information/location) at a time. 
In other words, the data interface does not support the so-called mass searches, which could be used to search for information from many places of use 
at a time. The following data searches are implemented in the data interface: 
• 
Search for location information 
• 
Search for contract information for the place of use 
• 
Search for measurement data of the place of use 
• 
Search for authorization information for the place of use

business processes in the data hub

Regarding party information, the information of all parties can be searched for at once. 
When using the information interface, the parties' rights to information are taken into account with the same rules as 
in the message interface. The party gets thisonly access the information to which the party has the right either through an agreement or authorization. To ensure data protection, the customer ID with which the agreement has been made must always be entered in the search. A single customer ID is also sufficient if the agreement has more than one customer. 
Datahub's data interface has its own documentation published in the service portal's 
Interface descriptions. 
In addition to the data interface, datahub offers parties the opportunity to run .csv-format 
control reports on their own data for data quality checking purposes. Control reports can be run on all of the party's own data by data set, including customer, 
location of use, contract and authorization data. For example, a party can run a control report on all of its own customer data, in which case Datahub returns a report on all of the customers active at the time given for the report, to whom the party running the report has the right either under the agreement or authorization.

3.1 
DH-100 Management of customer, utility and energy community information 
Customer and utility information are the most important basic information exchanged between the parties, which are 
stored in the Datahub database. This chapter describes the principles of maintaining and searching for this and energy community information in Datahub.

for example, to start if the place of use is new and the meter has not yet been installed.

When the point of use is "metered", i.e. when it is possible to start delivery, the distribution system operator activates 
by updating its status to "connected" or "disconnected" depending on whether it is started at the same time 
delivery or not. Updating to "connected" and "disconnected" state is done by switching and 
using disconnect events. Updating to "Removed from the system" status takes place 
with the deletion event of the place of use. Other status changes will be announced at the place of use 
with an update event.  
The distribution system operator can temporarily passivate the access point by changing its status to "under construction". 
This is how it works, e.g. in renovation sites, when it is temporarily not possible to start delivery to the place of use. 
The current sales contract is not automatically terminated when the place of use is changed to this one 
space, but the seller must agree on the matter with the customer if necessary. 
When delivery to the point of use can be started normally, its status in the data hub is "connected" or 
"truncated". Contracts and delivery can be made for the places of use in these premises 
start immediately ("switched on") or as soon as the point of use can be switched on ("switched off"). 
The distribution network operator sets the access point in the data hub to "disabled" when the access point 
taking it out of use is final, for example, when the distribution system operator terminates the subscription. 
The distribution system operator must ensure that the termination of the usage site contracts is notified 
to the datahub before notification of the removal of the place of use. When the place of use has been declared deleted 
of use, contracts can no longer be concluded for the place of use and its status can no longer be changed 
back e.g. 'switched on'. 
Usage slots created incorrectly in the data hub must be deleted from the data hub. To remove the place of use 
own deletion event is used. You can no longer use an incorrectly declared user ID 
reuse when creating a new location. The usage location information remains deleted in the data hub 
from the system as an opportunity. A location of use that has been removed from the system is not visible to the distribution system operator 
in addition to other parties, for example when searching for a user ID. If there is for the place of use 
had time to make transactions that have not yet taken effect before the error was detected, will 
these events must be canceled first, after which the place of use must be set to the state "deactivated. 
 
Contracts can be made for the place of use as soon as its information can be found in the data hub. Provided 
a new sales contract is made for the place of use while it is still in the state "under construction", but delivery 
cannot be started on the marked start date of the contract, the start date of the sales contract and 
the actual Connection date will differ. In these situations, the distribution system operator 
in the data hub, the connection notification indicated automatically changes the on the connection day 
the effective dates of the valid sales and network agreement to correspond to the connection date. Seller 
receives a notification about the update of the usage location information and the connection and this notification 
based on this, the seller must update the effective date to the connection date in his own system. 
Datahub also updates the effective date of the network contract, so the network company also ensures, 
that the effective date of the network contract in your own system is the same as the connection date. 
Datahub does not notify the parties of a change in the date of the contracts. The parties 
in this situation, no announcement should be made regarding the update of the effective date 
nor to datahub. If the state of the place of use is changed, for example during repairs, will

In addition to the point of use status, the distribution system operator must update other information about its own points of use to the 
datahub, excluding the point of use identifier, which must never be updated. The update must be made 
as soon as the data changes in the distribution system operator's own system. Datahub stores 
historical data of the point of use, i.e. the creation or modification time is always stored for the point of use data, 
which is taken into account when searching for the data according to the rights of the parties. 
The point of use property "heating depends on electricity" partly affects whether the parties have the right to 
disconnect the electricity to the point of use in winter (Network Service Terms VPE 2019, section 9.1.4). 
The distribution system operator is responsible for maintaining the data in Datahub. However, Datahub does not validate disconnection requests or notifications on this basis. 
The current and future seller of the point of use and the third party also have the opportunity to notify of 
changes to the point of use data. However, the point of use data reported to Datahub by the seller or third party is not automatically updated to Datahub, but is forwarded to the distribution system operator, who 
makes the actual update. The distribution system operator must respond to the update request by sending an 
update of the access point information to Datahub, which includes either the information provided by the seller/third party 
(the distribution system operator accepts the update request), or the 
access point information in its own system (the distribution system operator rejects the update request). If the distribution system operator decides

In terms of the functionality of the contract processes, there is a need to maintain a more reliable way to link these consumption and production usage sites together in addition to the address. This linking is done through the maintenance processes of the parallel usage site information by informing the consumption/production usage site of the identifier of the production/consumption usage site with which the consumption/production usage site is physically located in the same location. The link between the connected 
points of use is bidirectional, i.e. each point of use has information about the other linked (parallel) point of use. With the link, the parallel points of use are included in the netting calculations if the calculation conditions are met, and information about their inclusion in the calculations is stored in the points of use. The netting of metering data for parallel points of use is described in section 3.3.7. 
The Finnish retail market is moving to hourlyfrom measurement to 15-minute measurement (arm measurement) 
From 1 January 2023. The transition is carried out flexibly so that the notification of hourly measurement data is 
possible during the transition period. The transition period is specified in the Government Decree on Electricity 
on delivery and measurement in the transition provision. Due to the transition period, distribution system operators 
must be controlled by the time step (hour or 15 
minutes) per measurement point. The time step of the measurement of the place of use is updated with a separate time
with a step update event. The time step of production units and limit points is updated 
with the datahub user interface. The update also applies to the reactive energy of the measurement point. Datahub does not update 
from the time step of the possible parallel usage location measurement automatically, but by the network company 
you should always update the information for each place of use separately. Often parallel places of use 
are measured with the same meter, in which case the time steps are also the same. Sellers have to 
however, it is good to note that a different time step may occur at parallel places of use, if 
the distribution system operator has changed the time step to only one of the parallel usage locations. Time-
the step can be updated retroactively, but only for the time the balance window is open (11 days). 
Retrospective updating is not possible, however, if values ​​have already been reported for the measurement point previously 
with a time step for the time after the effective time of the update. In the event of an error, the datahub
the operator can perform a retrospective update for a maximum of the open time of the balance window 
from the distribution system operator's service request. 
From the point of view of Datahub's operation, it does not matter whether it is a construction site, event or other 
processing of temporary places of use takes place in the distribution system operator's internal processes. 
Distribution system operators have different operating methods for handling temporary usage locations. Provided 
the distribution system operator always sets up a new one in its own system at the temporary point of use 
place of use, the new place of use is reported to datahub according to the normal creation process. 
If, on the other hand, the distribution network operator uses one usage location ID and only updates the usage location 
according to the address, where the temporary place of use is located at any time, the corresponding is indicated 
change of address to the datahub with the update event of the location of use. The distribution system operator must here 
in this case, ensure that the location of use is not reported to datahub as disabled for so long, 
when it will be used again.

the customer's basic information is shared among all the market participants who have the customer 
contracts with. The customer's basic information includes only the information that is in the market 
what is necessary is maintained centrally and other information is maintained as part of the contract information 
per party. At a high level, the distribution is done in such a way that the customer's name and address are read as the customer's information 
identification information as well as contact and postal address information. In the case of business customers, contact and 
the information of the company's head office is used in the postal address information.

in this case, in the contract-specific information, the information of the location to which the contract applies is indicated.

for example, a company's department or place of business or a municipality's business. The same customer specification 
can be used when, in the case of a business customer, you want the company to appear on the contract 
auxiliary function name. The auxiliary name is not unique in its customer's datahub, because it uses the same one 
y code than the actual company to which the subsidiary name belongs. In order to avoid unnecessary information 
from multiple updating, special attention should be paid to the situation in which the information is 
what should be maintained in the customer's information and what information should be handled 
in the contract information.

3.1.2.1 
Customer type and identifier  
There are two types of customers in Datahub, which are consumer and business customers.  As business customers 
all legal entities (companies, associations, public actors) are processed and all are consumer customers 
natural persons. The customer is identified in the data hub with an identifier, which, depending on the customer type, is 
either personal identification number or y-identification number (or VAT identification number for foreign companies). Contracts can therefore 
report to datahub only in such a way that the customer data contains this identifier (special situations, 
where the party's own ID is used as an identifier, is described below). If a contract is made 
in the names of several customers, the information of all customers with their identifiers is reported, in which case the contract 
is connected to several customers in the data hub.  
In the case of foreign customers who do not yet have a Finnish personal identification number, it is possible 
the contract in this special situation informs datahub without an identifier, but then it must be notified 
customer's date of birth. In addition, the party's ID is reported to the datahub as the customer's ID 
identifier (so-called other identifier) ​​consisting of the seller's party identifier (GLN identifier) ​​and 
from the seller's customer ID. With the announcement of the new contract, the customer's created by the seller 
the identifier is also forwarded to the distribution system operator. Based on this, the seller and the distribution system operator 
can later identify the customer in the data hub. If the customer has a foreigner 
personal ID or an ID equivalent to this, it can be reported to datahub as the customer's additional ID 
in the field. 
It is the responsibility of the party that notified the agreement to update the customer's information in datahub as soon as 
personal identification number is available. After the update, all the customer's previous contracts are 
can be found using a new personal ID. Foreign customers are the only exception, when 
the contract can be reported to the consumer customer in datahub without the customer's identifier. 
The creation of anonymous customers in the data hub will be monitored.  
A private entrepreneur (more commonly known as a business name) is a business customer who is responsible 
personally from their contracts. All private entrepreneurs are granted a y-identification number 
when they register with the authorities. In the case of private traders, for business customers 
must be able to provide a personal identification number. In Datahub, private entrepreneurs are identified 
with the y code and the personal ID is entered in the customer's additional ID field. In this way, the customer can

3.1.2.2 
Correctness and maintenance of customer data 
The parties are responsible for the correctness of the customer information they provide to datahub. Datahub does not 
content validation of the information, such as checking whether the customer's name and social security number match each other. 
The parties must ensure that the name of the business customer is reported in the form it is 
in the official register (YTJ). In addition, it must be ensured that for a business customer in the customer information 
the stated postal address corresponds to the address of the main office stated in the official register (YTJ). 
Separate address information for the locations must be maintained in the contract information. 
The customer is created in datahub only as part of the contract processes. If sent by the party 
the customer in the contract notice cannot be found based on the identifier in datahub, let's create it 
as a new Customer record in datahub. If the customer can be found based on the identifier in the data hub, 
the contract to be notified is attached to the existing Customer-tiesupport. In addition to this, the customer 
the information is updated to match the customer information in the notification. If the contract is notified several times 
for the customer to be responsible for, i.e. there are more than one contractual partner in the party's contract notification, 
in datahub, several Customer records are attached to the contract. 
In Datahub, the main responsibility for maintaining customer information rests with the seller. They can update customer information 
sellers who have a valid contract with the customer. Customer information can be updated as a part 
contract processes or with a separate notification. In addition to this, the distribution system operator or a third party can 
sends a customer information update request to datahub, which is forwarded to the seller who is 
finally made a contract with the customer. This seller does the actual customer information 
update, because he can be assumed to have the most recent information about the customer. The seller can refuse 
about updating the information, if the seller considers that the update request is unwarranted or incorrect. The seller 
must respond to the update request by sending an update of the customer information to the data hub, which contains either 
information provided by the distribution system operator/3rd party (the seller accepts the update request), or in its own 
customer data in their system (the seller rejects the update request). If the seller does not respond 
to the update request within 2 business days, this is taken into account under the control of the datahub operator and
