3.5.1 
Initial data for the balance sheet 
Balance sheet data consists of structural data and measurement/time series data. Structurally 
the information is used to manage which party's balance sheet and which measurement area each measurement point is used for 
measurement data (measured consumption or production) are calculated by the data hub 
in balance sheet calculations. 
According to the Nordic balance sheet model, the distribution system operator's balance sheet is calculated 
by measurement area. Distribution system operators can divide their networks into one or more 
to the measurement range. Mainly, however, distribution system operators only have one measurement area. Below 
the figure below shows the information based on the balance sheet calculations in the data hub 
is performed. The responsibility for maintaining this information rests with the distribution system operator for sales contract information 
except. Technically, however, the data hub operator will manage the measurement areas 
data because this data has a significant and wide-ranging impact on other datahub data and 
processes, including balance sheet calculations and usage location information. In practice, we want to 
ensure that all necessary changes, such as deciding and adding measurement areas, 
is done in a controlled manner, taking into account all perspectives. 
The relations marked in blue are valid. This means that, for example, 
the loss seller of the measurement area may change over time and the system must be able to manage these 
changes in such a way that the History data is preserved. When interpreting the picture, it should be noted that in part 
of these relations, only one relation can be valid at a time, even if it is marked as multiplicity 
"1..*". Exact definitions of relationships can be found in the data standard. Relationships related to balance sheet information 
validity is determined based on the validity of the balance sheet information. It is also discussed in Datahub 
information on market balance areas, even though there is only one market balance area in use in Finland. 
This ensures that the data hub supports the general structure of the electricity market as much as possible 
for future needs.

of the day. Balance responsibility is transferred back to the seller (a new balance sheet is created) of the distribution system operator 
on the basis of the indicated switching moment. 
3.5.2 
Virtual production units 
Measurement area- and vendor-specific small-scale production, i.e. related to the production-type place of use 
production, is processed in NBS in such a way that a so-called virtual production unit, 
the production of which is calculated as the total small production per measurement area and vendor. Because of this 
the system must have vendor-, measurement area- and NBS-specific virtual 
production unit whenever the seller has balance sheet information for the place of use where the type of place of use is 
"production". In Datahub, virtual production units are managed in such a way that the virtual 
creation of production units, deletion and updates of validity periods do not require separate user 
measures. 
The virtual production unit is treated in the NBS model like any other production unit. Thus 
for the virtual production unit, an ID, name, according to NBS, must be assigned to the system 
type of production and capacity. Capacity maintenance, for example, the power of production equipment 
summing is not meaningful, as this would require calculating a new capacity 
at best daily, so it must be possible to set a certain predefined value as capacity. 
The name of the virtual production unit is generated automatically, for example, the measuring range, vendor

(NBS)-Production type

Production unit ID

The validity period is not updated, but a new 
virtual production unit is created if necessary. 
Production unit-Seller 
The validity period is determined based on the validity periods of the balance information 
so that the relation is valid whenever the seller has at least one 
balance information for the point of use that is related to the corresponding 
metering area and has a production type that corresponds to the balance settlement type of the production unit. If necessary, the relation has several different 
time intervals.

FIGURE 444444 DATA ON IMBALANCE SETTLEMENT CONNECTIONS 
Imbalance settlement time series serve as the basis for the imbalance settlement performed by eSett. In Datahub, the 
balance settlement type determines the purpose of the imbalance settlement time series in the imbalance settlement. 
The imbalance settlement method determines whether the imbalance settlement data is based on measured or otherwise 
determined, i.e. profiled data. In Datahub, profiled measurement data is all 
measurement data that is related to a point of use whose measurement method is readingmeasurement or 
unmetered. It should be noted that the method of measuring the place of use can change in practice 
several times and these changes with validity information must be taken into account 
in balance sheet calculations. For example, consumption is calculated for the seller's profiled sum delivery 
only and only for those periods when the measurement method of the place of use is "reading measurement" or 
"unmeasured". 
Not all combinations of balance settlement method and type are in use. The NBS model allows, for example, both 
measured and profiled (network) losses, although only measured losses are used in Finland. 
Profiled balance sheet information in Finland is only used for sum deliveries and 
for self-use of production units. For places of use, the method of measuring the place of use determines it, 
which balance sheet method is used to calculate the consumption/production of the respective site of use.  
The balance sheet connection is, in principle, the datahub's equivalent to the MEC defined by eSett (Market 
Entity Connection) [4]. Datahub's balance sheet connection is a concept that defines a balance sheet time series 
the related balance settlement method and type and connects the time series to market participants and production data

From the balance settlement time series processed by Datahub, the balance deviations of the measurement areas (MGA 
Imbalance) and confirmed limit point sums (MGA Exchange confirmation) are calculated in eSett 
in the system. The purpose of balancing is to manage situations where various rounding, 
due to calculation and data exchange errors, the limit point sum of the measurement range does not match 
to the sum of productions in the measurement area, deliveries by sellers and losses in the measurement areas. In these 
the balance deviation calculated in situations is recorded by the open supplier of the balance deviation of the measurement area 
for delivery. The balance deviation is calculated as the sum of calculations 1-7 in the table below, signs 
taking into account. Since the losses of the measurement areas (calculation 7) are calculated as the sum of calculations 1-6, should 
the calculated imbalance should always be zero under normal circumstances. Balance deviation is provided by eSett 
separately for the open balance window of the preliminary balance deviation and the final one 
for the day on which the imbalance closed.

amount information according to the type and method of balance settlement. The table below shows the data hub 
calculated sum calculations used in Finland's balance sheet. 
The information on the blue-gray background is reported to eSett for balance settlement. Measurement areas 
when calculating losses, the principle is that losses are calculated from the data reported to eSett 
based on and not on the basis of sum calculations of measurement areas. Losses are calculated, for example 
on the basis of individual limit point sums instead of the total limit point sum of the measurement area 
to avoid possible rounding errors. Rounding errors could cause unnecessary 
balance deviations in eSett's calculations. 
With the transition to the quarterly balance sheet, Datahub will calculate the total information of the balance sheet every quarter 
with a time step. Regarding hourly measurements, in the balance sheet calculation, the series of hours are first counted as own 
into series of sums. The hourly sum series are then divided by four and added together 
with individual sum sets.

3.5.8 
Balance sheet calculations outside the balance sheet window 
Primarily, balance sheet calculations are calculated in the data hub by the official eSett 
for the needs of the balance sheet. However, the results of balance sheet calculations have other uses 
in addition to the official balance sheet. For example, losses in the measurement area are a significant expense item 
for the network company and the exact amount of losses is monitored in the network companies also in the balance sheet window 
outside time. Datahub will be the primary data warehouse for measurement and 
for balance sheet information, so it is natural that all up-to-date and corrected measurement data and about them 
the calculated calculation results are available from datahub for all data. 
The official balance sheet always closes when the balance sheet window closes, and then in the official one 
the information calculated in the balance sheet and reported to eSett can no longer be changed. Balance window

3.6 
DH-600 Handling of balance errors 
Handling of balance errorsy in the datahub is based on the Energy industry's guideline "Those left on the balance sheet 
handling of errors after balance sheet closing" [3]. Balance sheet errors are based on all 
to processes that change the balance sheet data of the seller or the measurement data of the place of use in the balance sheet window 
outside. Processes that produce balance errors are: 
• 
DH-211 Notification of measurement data / correction of measurement errors outside the balance window7 
• 
DH-300 - the so-called contract processes described in chapter 3.2.5 retroactive contract processes, 
where changes are made to the validity of contracts outside the balance sheet window (retroactive 
contract initiations, terminations and cancellations) 
• 
Performed manually by the datahub operator at the operators' separate request 
balance sheet corrections. 
It should be noted that with the introduction of the data hub, separate readings of measured measurement data 
the smoothing calculation is not performed. Those based on the annual usage estimate of metered objects 
updating measurement data with reading-based measurement data and the need it causes 
corrections between the parties will be processed in the same balance sheet error processing process 
like other balance corrections. 
 
7 for reading measurement targets (use locations where the measurement method is other than "continuous measurement"). 
measurement data is always reported retrospectively, which creates balance errors.

3.6.1 
The process of calculating and processing balance sheet errors 
 
FIGURE 494949 BALANCE ERROR CORRECTION PROCESS DIAGRAM 
The correction of balance errors works in datahub according to the diagram above. Datahub initially configures 
Location-specific vendor balance sheet information with information at the time of calculation. Balance sheet information is understood here 
in addition to the definition in section 3.2.5, also according to the time step measured at the place of use 
energies for the corresponding period for which the seller has balance responsibility. The calculation is performed only for them 
for places of use for which new measurement devices outside the balance window have been registered for the calculation period 
changes in balance sheet information that have not yet been taken into account in previous calculation times. 
The location-specific time series compiled from the balance sheet data at the time of calculation is called 
"measured information". After this, the result of the calculation is compared to the so-called 
to the balance sheet time series, which is based on the information reported and locked in the balance sheet or already 
to the data corrected in the previous calculation. More precisely, the measured information is compared 
to the information corrected in the previous calculation for the time period that was also processed in the previous one 
in calculation. In other respects, i.e. to the extent that the time period in question has not been included in the previous one 
in the calculation, the measured information is compared to the one valid at the closing time of the balance window 
information. Any differences in the comparison are recorded as balance sheet errors and the seller's correction in euros

3.6.2 
Balance errors caused by corrections of measurement data 
Regarding corrections of measurement data, balance errors are recorded only for those sellers who have responsibility 
regarding correcting the invoicing of the customer's sales contract in accordance with chapter 3.3.4. Measurement errors 
regarding the balance sheet errors are always corrected for the seller who has during the measurement error's effective period and 
contract information valid at the time of calculation of balance sheet errors. In other words, mino typing error 
correct for those sellers who are in the balance sheet due to their own mistake in their own balance sheet 
responsible for the consumption of the place of use without the actual right (contractual information) to bill 
customer for consumed electricity. The distribution system operator must always report the corrected measurement data in full 
for the effective period of the error and not only for the period for which the seller invoices the customer 
the repair. Thus, it is ensured that the data hub always has correct and up-to-date information 
also available to customers and third parties. 
3.6.3 
Balance error of measurement range loss 
In addition to places of use, balance errors are also related to losses in the measurement area. Loss balance errors 
is recorded in the balance sheet of the loss seller of the measurement area. Losses are also affected outside the balance sheet window 
reported corrections of measurement data as well as such corrections of balance sheet information where the place of use remains 
without a salesperson or for a place of use without a salesperson, a salesperson is added. Losses of measurement areas 
the balance error time series can be calculated by summing all the usage locations in the measurement area 
balance sheet errors together, taking into account the sign of the balance sheet errors. The balance time series of losses is formed 
like the place of use, of the values ​​locked in the balance sheet/losses in the previous balance sheet error calculation 
of values ​​updated according to measured data. Balance error calculation of losses in the measurement area 
"measured information" can be calculated inversely by calculating the balance errors of the losses and the balance time series 
values ​​together and finally the measured data calculated in this way is stored in the balance time series after the calculation 
for. The loss seller of the measurement area is not notified separately of balance error information from those places of use, 
whose balance sheet errors have caused a balance sheet error of losses. In other words, the loss seller gets the information 
only from the total error of the losses. Errors in the balance of losses are not reported to the seller whose losses 
sales in the measurement area have ended.

3.6.4 
Balance sheet errors regarding netting and energy companies 
Netting and energy community calculations are performed as soon as netting or energy community 
measurement data is delivered to the relevant point of use. This also applies to situations where delivery is required 
measurement data is directed outside the open balance window. Possible in the calculation of balance errors 
changed netting calculation or energy community calculation values ​​are compared in the balance sheets 
to the closed original values ​​or to the values ​​of the previous balance error calculation. The treatment is the same 
regardless of the distribution method of the energy community's surplus energy (SMA or SMB). Balance errors 
is formed if the netting and energy community calculation values ​​have changed in the balance sheets 
after closing. 
3.6.5 
Execution of balance sheet error calculations 
Balance error calculations are only performed at separate times by the data hub operator. Otherwise 
that is, automatic, such as scheduled, balance error calculations are not performed. There will be balance errors 
to repair in accordance with ET's instructions for each place of use, 3 years retroactively twice 
per year. The calculation of balance sheet errors can also be started from the market party's separate account 
on request, if the balance error is large and it is wanted to be dealt with quickly. Calculation can be done 
if necessary, perform for a single measurement area or place of use. All repair billing 
the balance sheet and balance sheet error data that were the basis are stored as historical data from time to time 
for revisions. Thus, the data hub always has information on what was initially reported to the balance sheet and 
how this information has been corrected later in each balance error calculation run.

3.7 
DH-710 and DH-720 Product information maintenance and search 
3.7.1 
Product information 
Datahub enables the maintenance and forwarding of product information for various needs. For sellers 
can make a sales contract with a product corresponding to the online product of the place of use, shall 
distribution system operators maintain the data of their own transmission products according to the structure below. 
Sellers also need network product information for invoicing the electricity supply contract.  
Sellers can maintain sales product information for their own needs and with other operators 
in accordance with the agreements they have made. The sales product is not forwarded to the distribution network operator or a third party 
without separate authorization from the seller. 
Product and price information must be reported and can be retrieved via the automated interface DH-
700 according to events. Information is provided in searches for location data and contract processes 
only the product ID, in which case the aforementioned should be used to clarify the product structure 
interface. If necessary, you can specify more than one product for the contract. Regarding price information 
the prices of online products are public and thus they must be reported to datahub and they are 
datahub available to all parties. Regarding sales products, the price information is in the datahub 
available only to those parties to whom the seller has authorized access to the information. The customer can't 
gives the 3rd party authorization for price information.

In the structure above, the product can be, for example, "Time transfer", which has two product components: 
"Day transfer" and "Night transfer". A calendar time series is a time series whose time step value can be either 0 
or 1. If the value is 1, it means that the relevant time step is applied 
product component. The calendar time series must be created for each year separately, because the calendar 
may depend, for example, on public holidays, which are timed differently each year. In the calendar time series 
the transition to summer and winter time and the extra day in leap years must also be taken into account. 
Calendar time series must be announced by the end of September at the latest. The price time series tells 
price for each time step. 
3.7.2 
Establishing the product 
When creating product information, all necessary information about the structure of the product is reported in the product information. 
Once the product structure has been declared, it cannot be changed. Structural information is indicated by one 
event and in this product creation event, the party indicates whether it is related to the product 
single price or price time series. If the type of the price of the declared product is BG01=Price, 
the product is only approved when the price of the product has been reported to the datahub with a separate price information 
with an update notification. The product is not active until the price is announced. The price of the product cannot 
update retroactively. If the product's price type is a price-time series, the product is active immediately 
after the creation of the product, even if the price time series has not yet been announced. Price time series 
can be reported a maximum of one year retroactively.  
The product can also contain a calendar time series. A calendar time series defines those moments in time, 
in which case the product component of the product (night or day electricity) is valid. The calendar time series is announced 
with the same event as the price time series.    
Datahub's products consist of one or more components. For each product 
one's own component is declared, even if the component in question is used in the rest of the party 
in the product. With this, different prices for components can be announced for each product.  
Product names and components can be reported to datahub in different waysyesterday. The languages ​​are Finnish, Swedish and 
English. The combination of the product ID and the component ID and the product ID is 
be individual. If the product is cancelled, the product ID cannot be used again.  
3.7.3 
Maintenance of the product's structural information 
The parties can maintain their own products. The product's structural information contains information about the product 
and product components. Structural information can be used to maintain product names and 
product component name and tax rate. If necessary, the product can also be given an expiration date. 
When the end date is announced, the product remains expired in datahub and no changes can be made to it anymore 
then.  
The parties cannot maintain the product structure after it has been announced. That is, the product cannot be added or 
components cannot be removed from it after it has been deployed. If such 
changes need to be made, it should be done by announcing a new product to datahub and deciding 
existing legacy product.

3.7.4 
Reporting a price or price time series 
When the party needs to change the prices of the product, it is done with its own notification.  
The parties always announce the new prices to datahub at least one month before the price of the product 
entry into force. A new Price Notice always determines the new price of the old valid price 
effective date to the previous day. If the price needs to be updated retroactively, e.g. error 
due to this, the party informs the operator of this, who makes the necessary update. A party can 
only change the prices announced for the future and this is done by replacing the old price 
new.    
The prices reported to Datahub are reported both with and without VAT. Thus 
it is easier for other parties to use exact prices in customer invoicing. Taxable 
calculating the price from the tax-free price can cause differences in decimal precision and this has 
impact on invoices sent to the customer. 
There are also products where payments are based on different conditions and calculation formulas, 
where more billing criteria are used than the realized electricity consumption of a certain hour. Such 
can be, for example, power-based products where the payments are based on a certain interval or 
to several maximum measured electric power. For these products, price information is provided 
to datahub, however, the unit prices of the product. 
3.7.5 
Searches for product and price information 
Market participants can search for product information and product price information from datahub. 
The distribution system operator's product information is public and searchable by all parties. Seller's product information 
can apply for those parties who have a party authorization given by the seller for product information. 
The search for product information is divided into two different search events. You will apply at the second application event 
structural information of the product and price and price and calendar time series information on the other.  
With the structural information search event, product information is always requested by party, but search 
can also be refined based on the product ID. The search can also be specified if desired 
only search for valid information or historical information. 
In addition to party information, price information is searched based on the product or product component. Search 
can be limited by giving a time interval according to which price, price-time series or calendar time series data 
applied for.

3.8 
DH-730 and DH-740 Declaration and search of invoice line information 
3.8.1 
Invoice line information 
Sellers and distribution system operators can, if they wish, transmit invoice line data via the data hub. 
Invoice line information can be used, for example, when the party has agreed with the customer 
that the customer receives one bill for both electricity sales and transmission. In this case, the other party 
can inform the biller of all the billable data of the usage location using the bill line data 
to the party. The party that delivers the invoice line data to datahub verifies the invoice line data 
when forming, that the information is forwarded to the right recipient. It is indicated in the invoice line information 
in addition to the data of the sending party, the party ID of the receiving party and when there is 
it is a pass-through invoicing, including the contract ID of the receiving party. This is information that 
the parties get through the contract processes. If, for example, the distribution system operator delivers to the seller 
calline data, the distribution system operator must be able to form the line data of the network contract 
to the right recipient, taking into account a possible change of seller.  
 
In the example picture, the contract of seller B starts on May 1, 2019. Online contract not in case of change of seller 
change If the distribution system operator has agreed with both sellers on network pass-through billing, 
the distribution system operator must ensure that invoice line information is no longer sent to seller A on 1 May 2019 
from the starting billing period. 
Invoice line information can also be used when forwarding billing information to an invoicing provider 
to the service provider. If invoice line information is reported to the service provider, then not to the recipient 
there is no contract ID of the party. The parties must agree before the invoice line information is delivered 
with each other on the transfer of information and informs the party authorization between the parties for billing information 
in the user interface of the parties. In the user interface, the authorizing party selects the authorized person and informs 
validity period for the authorization.  The party authorization covers all between the authorizing parties 
count lines.  Receipt of invoice lines can still be delegated to another party. That is, if 
the distribution network operator authorizes seller A to receive the invoice lines, seller A can still commission 
to the service provider of forwarding own invoice lines C. The customer cannot give authorization for invoice information 
to a 3rd party. 
The party reports the invoice line information to the data hub after it has created it in its own 
in their system in accordance with their own invoicing processes. Invoice line information is reported 
with the accuracy of the product component. For example, an electrical product is reported as a separate line 
possible basic payment component and energy component. It is stated in the invoice information 
separately for the entire invoice period, but also for each invoice line, the period for that line 
concerns. In the billing period, the billing lines may have, for example, some subsequently corrected ones

to electricity consumption data. The principle of these authorizations is described in the figure below 
with the number 1. 
2. Authorizations or mandates given to each other by the Datahub parties, by which the parties 
give other parties the right to their own information or the right to perform a role 
according to the task. The principle of these mandates and party authorizations is described below 
in the picture with numbers 2 (orders and party authorizations given by the seller) and 3

The authorizations given by the customer are always site-specific and must be given 
validity period, which is a maximum of 2 years. The validity period must correspond to the intended use. 
For example, purposes 1b and 1c of the table entitle the grantee to the same information, 
but the validity periods of the authorizations differ because the purposes of use are different. Authorizations 
also provide a measure of justicefor a different period of time depending on the type of authorization, 
if the customer has had a contract for the point of use. If the customer has authorized a new vendor, 
for example, with the authorization type Request for quotation, the vendor has the right to the information for two days, but 
the metering data will be received retroactively for one year. If a customer who is just moving to a 
new point of use gives authorization, for example, to a new vendor, the authorization will also be stored in this 
situation for the customer and point of use. In this case, the customer's information shows that the authorization has been 
given in relation to this particular point of use. In this case, the customer cannot give authorization for 
metering data, because they have not previously been a customer of the point of use and therefore do not own 
metering data, until the date of the move. If the customer moves out of the point of use for which they have given authorizations, the authorizations will be automatically terminated in Datahub upon moving out. 
Similarly, authorizations provided by the customer are automatically terminated as soon as the customer information is updated to indicate that the customer is “encrypted”. 
The customer issues an authorization to the seller or a third party, after which the party can retrieve the information specified in the authorization from Datahub. In accordance with the Electricity Market Act and the current Data Protection Regulation, authorization from the consumer customer must come directly to Datahub by the consumer customer himself. Therefore, the consumer customer always issues the authorization himself using strong authentication

3.9.2 
Party authorizations and assignments between parties 
Authorizations between parties have two different purposes. With a party authorization, the parties allow the other party to obtain information that is not possible to obtain without the authorization. An assignment, in turn, grants permission to act in Datahub on behalf of the other party. 
3.9.2.1 
Party authorizations 
Party authorizations between parties are required for receiving invoice line information and for product information reported by the 
seller. Party authorization is granted in the parties' user interface by selecting the 
desired party and the function to be authorized. Party authorization can be granted to several 
parties at the same time.

delivery). The authorized party gets the rights to the data hub's data in accordance with the information in the assignment and 
to processes (such as delivery of measurement data). Market participants notify the data hub operator

to the system. The parties can view assignment information in the datahub user interface.

the party can request a copy of the changed information.

the party has an agreement to perform some task. The assignment can therefore be given to someone else 
to the seller, the distribution system operator or a 3rd party, in which case each party can act in several different ones 
role towards the data hub. Assignments between the parties can no longer be forwarded 
to a third party. The party that received the mandate can therefore no longer give the mandate itself 
to a new party for the same information or function for which he himself received an assignment. Neither 
the party cannot forward the authorization received from the customer to a third party 
to the party. Events related to party information (DH-9XX) and customer and usage location information 
update request events (DH-112, DH-113 and DH-124) cannot be delegated to another 
to the party.

3.10 
DH-900 Party data maintenance 
Party data is maintained in the data hub both for the needs of the parties and the data hub operator 
needs. The parties need each other's contact information and billing information. Yestahub operator 
needs information about the parties, related to service contracts. As part of the service contract process 
the operator will find out the necessary mandatory information from the party.  
Although information is transmitted from one party to another via the data hub, there may be situations where direct 
contact between the parties is necessary. For these needs, in datahub's party information 
the parties' contact information for contracts, invoicing, measurement data, balance sheet errors is maintained 
and in relation to collection. For these types of contact information, the contact person and their phone number are indicated 
or email address.  
Datahub maintains information about the party's billing addresses, i.e. the addresses to which the other parties 
or the datahub operator can send the invoice. Datahub maintains different billing addresses 
for needs, i.e. invoicing of balance errors, joint invoicing and connection and disconnection costs 
for invoicing. Regarding invoicing channels, the parties have at their disposal a paper invoice and an online invoice.  
New parties are always established in the datahub by the datahub operator. The parties may 
however, after this, the parties maintain their own data provided by datahub 
in the user interface. Datahub announces the registration of new parties, the termination of parties and 
the parties' information is updated for all datahub parties.  The distribution system operator can 
in connection with the notification, also the necessary information for sending balance error invoices. 
Party information can be searched with a separate search transaction either through the GLN of the requested party
a single organization with an ID or several based on the role of the requested party 
party. Party information can also be searched in the user interface offered to parties.  
Information about the parties is maintained according to the category diagram below.

3.11 
Structural changes in the measurement area 
This chapter describes the situations where individual measurement points are moved from one measurement area to another 
or where the entire management of the measurement area is transferred from one distribution system operator to another. 
The descriptions have been made primarily from the perspective of the data hub. This chapter does not cover them 
situations that belong to normal market processes, where for the existing measurement area 
new measurement points are added or measurement points are taken out of use there. 
In connection with structural changes in measurement areas, there is a need to exchange information about the changes 
between market participants. Regarding the structural changes described in this chapter, it is 
however, from relatively rare processes and these changes are also often very large 
number of places of use (possibly even hundreds of thousands of places of use).  Described below 
processes are not carried out with normal market messages, but a separate one is used for information exchange 
data transfer method based on a transfer file.  The parties form a data hub with the support of the operator 
csv file to be moved. Using this file, the datahub operator and 
the distribution system operators participating in the transfer will make the necessary changes.  
It is worth noting that when the usage locations are transferred to the control of another distribution system operator 
without exception, the distribution network operators must always implement a separate data hub among themselves 
data conversion, where data is transferred from the current network operator to a new one. In terms of change 
overall, it is important that the new distribution system operator can secure the data hub and its own 
in connection with the change of data correspondence in the information system. 
The changes described in part in this chapter also affect eSett's systems. This is why eSett 
you must also agree on the change in advance before carrying it out. In general, the measurement range 
structural changes should be agreed well in advance with the datahub organization so that 
a controlled implementation of the change can be implemented. 
The processes also involve the transfer of network contracts to another network operator. In these changes 
network operators should note that changes must be made in accordance with the network service conditions. 
The changes always also affect the sellers of the respective measurement area, so precise communication 
of such situations is of paramount importance.

new network company. In Datahub's data model, this applies to the connection between the metering area and the distribution system operator (see image below).

PICTURE 555555 TRANSFER OF MANAGEMENT OF THE ENTIRE METERING AREA 
The transfer of management of the metering area to another network company does not in itself affect the other 
structure of the metering area. For example, the usage points belonging to the metering area will be transferred as such to the management of the new 
network company. Information will be stored in Datahub about which network operator has been managing the metering area at any given time. 
When the management of a metering area is transferred from one distribution system operator to another, the following 
procedures are involved: 
• 
Ending the management of the metering area for the current distribution system operator and starting it for the new distribution system operator from a certain point in time. 
• 
Transfer of network agreements from the current distribution system operator to the new distribution system operator. . 
Network agreements are transferred as such from the current network company to the new one. 
• 
Calculation of imbalance errors for the metering area for the current distribution system operator. 
The procedures related to the transfer of metering areas from one party to another are always initiated by the Datahub operator. The Distribution System Operator does not have the right to directly control which metering areas are under the management of the relevant distribution system operator in the user interface provided by Datahub. 
3.11.1.1 
Transfer of network contracts to a new distribution system operator 
When the operator initiates the transfer of the metering area, the 
valid metering point, contract and product information of all metering area usage points shall be reported to the new distribution system operator for confirmation.

This is done by generating a report from Datahub on the usage points included in the transfer. The report

distribution system operator for those network agreements that will come into force 
in the future.

The new distribution system operator must ensure that it has reported its new product information to the 
datahub before updating the information. If the new distribution system operator needs to update other 
network agreement information, such as the contract billing method, it must update this with a separate 
contract information update event after the operator has made the transfer for each usage point. 
With the transfer of network agreements, the rights to the information of the corresponding network agreements are transferred to the 
new distribution system operator. The boundary points are manually transferred from one metering area to another 
after the actual transfer event. 
3.11.1.2 
Transfer of rights to the new distribution system operator 
When the management of a metering area is transferred to another distribution system operator, the new distribution system operator will have the right to the information of all boundary points, production units and usage points in the metering area and the 
network agreements affected by the transfer. The new distribution system operator also has the right to the change history of all this information that has been registered in the datahub. Thus, the new distribution system operator also has the right to this change information from the time of the event when it itself was not responsible for the management of the metering area in question. The current distribution system operator's right to the information ends on the day when management of the metering area is transferred to another network company. 
The transfer of management of the metering area must also be taken into account in terms of the exchange of information in market processes. Information exchange related to market processes is carried out with the new distribution system operator for all metering area information from the time when ownership of the metering area is transferred to the new distribution system operator. 
3.11.1.3 
Rights to point-of-use information 
According to the data model, metering points are not directly related to the distribution system operator. The right to the metering points and their information is always established through the metering area. Thus, a change in the ownership of the metering area will also transfer ownership of the data for the usage points. 
The new distribution system operator of the metering area will have the right to the usage point data for the entire 
history of the usage pointfrom time. 
3.11.1.4 
Balance statement 
The transfer of control of the measurement area to another party does not directly affect itself 
for balance settlement calculations, as the measurement points do not move from one measurement area to another. A situation where 
measurement points move from one measurement area to another, is described separately in chapter 3.11.2. Information

Calculation of balance sheet errors

change. This is due to the fact that the invoicing of balance errors is the responsibility of the distribution system operator and

balance error calculations can be performed until the day when responsibility for the measurement area is transferred to a new one 
to the party. This should be possible from a general calculation performed on the entire market 
separately. This ensures that the current distribution system operator does not have to wait for months 
handling of balance errors, for example, in cases where the current distribution system operator 
business ends completely for the company in question. The transfer of the measurement area and related 
after a separate calculation of balance errors, the new distribution system operator is responsible for all new ones 
of balance errors throughout the history of the measurement area. Therefore, from the point of view of the data hub, the former 
balance sheet errors affecting the management period of the network company, which are detected and registered only after the transfer 
after, are always recorded to the new distribution system operator. However, online companies can of course 
mutually agree separately on which of the companies is financially responsible for these afterwards 
of detected errors.

3.11.2 
Division and merger of measurement areas 
This chapter discusses the situations in which control of the measurement area is maintained at the same time 
with the network operator, but one or more measurement points (location of use, border point or production unit) 
is moved to another measurement area. The things described in this chapter also apply in the situation when 
the measurement area is divided and in connection with the division a completely new measurement area is created for which 
measurement points are moved. The measurement points can either be transferred to another of the same network company 
to a measurement area or to a measurement area completely under the control of another grid company. Datahub 
in the information model, these changes concern the connection between the measurement area and the measurement points (see 
picture below). Datahub will store information about which measurement area the measurement point belongs to 
heard at any time. 
 
FIGURE 575757 TRANSFER OF MEASUREMENT POINTS FROM MEASUREMENT AREA TO ANOTHER 
To the extent that the management of certain places of use and their online contracts is transferred to another 
for the network company, the same principles as for rights and information exchange are followed 
beforeis described in this chapter. 
Next, we go through the necessary measures for each type of measurement point separately. 
3.11.2.1 
Places of use 
Moving locations to another measurement area should always be agreed on well in advance, at least 
monthly in advance before the transfer with datahub staff. If the places of use are transferred to another 
to the network operator's measurement area, the procedure is the same as in the situation where all the measurement area

Cut-off points 
In Datahub, the border points are always between two specific measurement areas. Datahub doesn't have it 
it is possible to change separately both measurement areas to which the limit point is connected. Practically 
when part of the measurement area moves to another measurement area, new ones must be created in the data hub 
border points between these two measurement ranges related to the case. In these situations, no 
basically, there is no need to decide on existing border points. If, on the other hand, two measuring areas 
merges, in practice the boundary points between these two measurement areas must be determined. 
The management of border points is directly the responsibility of the distribution system operators, and the distribution system operators can 
perform the necessary actions in these respects in the user interface provided by datahub. 
3.11.2.3 
Production units 
The distribution system operator can create new production units in the user interface provided by datahub. 
However, the processing of production units differs from border points in that the measurement areas 
in the changes, the termination and creation of the production unit cannot be applied. Production units 
otherwise, the existing production facility would have several GSRN identifiers and 
the measurement data would be divided into several measurement time series for the production plant in question. 
The transfer of the production unit to another measurement area is always done by the data hub operator. 
The procedure also requires changes in eSett's system, and the datahub operator is compatible with these 
about making changes with eSett. 
3.11.2.4 
Balance statement 
The transfer of measurement points from one measurement area to another affects the balance settlement calculations. 
However, changes in measurement areas do not require separate manual steps 
in connection with balance sheet calculations. The balance sheet calculations are defined in such a way that the calculation takes 
automatically takes into account the measurement area to which each measurement point is connected at any given time. 
Changes in the measurement areas are reflected in the calculation results of the balance sheet, just like the measurement areas 
in losses as losses changed. In connection with changes in measurement areas, it is always good to be more precise 
monitor the results of the calculations, as possible errors in the processing of changes can have an impact 
significantly to these results. On the other hand, this is also a good way to detect these possible errors. 
3.11.2.5 
Calculation of balance sheet errors 
In the calculation of balance errors, the transfer of the place of use to another measurement area should be taken into account 
correspondingly to when the distribution system operator managing the measurement area changes (see chapter 3.11.1.5).

3.12 
Customer access to own data 
Datahub will offer customers a user interface, the so-called customer portal, where 
customers can see information about themselves registered in datahub. In the customer portal, the customer can 
see the measurement data, contract data and other data of their usage locations. The customer sees everything 
his own information, regardless of which network company's territory his places of use are or who 
sells electricity to them. In addition, the customer can look at which companies, which data and for which period 
he has given authorization and if he wishes, the customer can change this authorization information. Provided 
the customer adds new authorizations or removes existing ones, datahub sends a notification to them 
to parties whose authorizations the customer has maintained. The customer can delete via the customer portal 
"encrypted" mark from own data. The handling of an "encrypted" customer is described in more detail in the chapter 
3.1.2. 
In 2017, a new national suomi.fi service was introduced in Finland, which is aimed at 
for all citizens. The customer's access to the datahub's customer portal is organized by the respective service 
through. In the Suomi.fi service, citizens can centrally see registered information about themselves 
in the registers and authorizes other citizens to manage their own affairs. in the Suomi.fi service 
companies can also authorize individuals to access company information. The customer can use the above 
said authorizations between persons and between persons and companies, including datahub 
customer portalin use. The Population Register Center is responsible for the development of the Suomi.fi service.  
Below is described the process of how to create access for the customer to the service offered by datahub and that 
through to the customer-specific information contained in the datahub.  
 
IMAGE 606060 CUSTOMER ACCESS TO THEIR OWN DATA 
The customer can access their own information through the following steps: 
1. The customer switches to the Suomi.fi service using an internet browser. 
2. The customer is identified by strong means of identification (for example, TUPAS or 
mobile certificate). 
3. The customer opens the "My electricity data" view in the Suomi.fi service, which shows limited 
some information about the customer registered in datahub and from which the customer can log in to datahub 
to the customer portal.

3.13 
Reporting required by the Energy Efficiency Act 
According to the Energy Efficiency Act, the seller of electricity must deliver to the person connected to the distribution network 
to the end-user customer once a year free of charge and properly report this energy 
of use. The law requires, among other things, the presentation of consumption data for the past 3 years, 
comparison of the customer's actual electricity use with other similar customers and information 
on measures to improve energy efficiency. Datahub will compile a user group-specific one 
anonymized sum-level consumption and small-scale production data that can be used by electricity sellers 
comparison data required by the Energy Efficiency Act in its own customer service 
in forming. A more detailed description of this information and the data transfer method will be determined 
in more detail in a later project phase. Possible delivery methods are for example in the chapter 
The data interface described in 2.5, the open data interface maintained by Fingrid or in quantitative format 
report.

3.14 
Repairs performed by the Datahub operator 
The main rule in the data hub is that the information stored in the data hub always comes from market participants. There is 
however, there are situations where the parties cannot update information in the data hub through normal processes 
and support from the datahub operator is required. In this case, the operator performs the necessary 
on behalf of either a party or end customer of the process, with own broader access rights. 
Examples of the most common repair processes are described in the following chapters.  
3.14.1 
Corrections related to contract processes 
With regard to contract processes, it has been described in relation to retroactive notices of contracts that if 
between the start date of the retroactive sales contract and the time of notification, the place of use has 
valid sales contracts of more than one different seller, the parties cannot agree with each other 
agree on a retroactive contract. In this case, the situation remains for the operator to figure out and 
to be repaired. The operator will clarify the situation related to this repair chain from the parties and leave it 
along to make repairs. Depending on the situation, the operator will cancel any contracts and also 
notify the termination, if necessary, of the remaining contract. To be done by the operator 
datahub does not send notifications to the parties about contract cancellations. If the operator this 
terminates the sales contract according to the repair chain, notification DH-331 is sent to the seller in question 
according to the process.   
In accordance with the normal process flow, contract terminations are never notified retroactively, 
except in case of meter removal. However, if the party needs to correct the contractual situation so, 
that a contract should be terminated retroactively, the operator is notified, who can do this 
retroactive termination (for example bankruptcy situations of the end customer). Retrospective decision 
can be made for both sales and online contracts. Retrospective actions made by the operator 
notices of contract terminations are normally sent to the other parties and also to it 
to the party whose contract the operator has terminated. 
Corrections to contract information are usually also accompanied by corrections to balance sheet information. Repair situations 
during the investigation, the operator also finds out from the parties the situation of the balance sheet information and does the necessary 
corrections to balance sheet information based on information received from the parties. Balance sheet informationno corrections will be sent 
notices to the parties.  
In the future, the Datahub operator will also handle those notified to the operator by the distribution system operator 
sales contract disputes. Disputing the contract is described in chapter 3.2.4.4. Provided 
the operator completes the dispute of the contract, sends his own notice of the disputed contract 
to the seller with reason code AR05 - Denying the contract.  
In the data conversion, the initial data is brought to the data hub. Not all information imported in data conversion can be 
to process information imported in accordance with datahub's processes with the same rules. By way of illustration 
contract cancellations. In Datahub's processes, rules have been created for cancellations as to what 
happens to previous contracts. For contracts imported through data conversion, no 
there is no previous information in datahub, so contracts imported through data conversion cannot be used normally 
cancel according to the cancellation process. If the parties need to cancel the data conversion

3.15 
Process chains in the datahub system 
Processes that have a clear dependency on each other have been created uniformly in the datahub system 
process chains. Process chains allow us to create pre-defined 
entities in which all processes in the process chain must be completed to the end of the chain 
to process. Monitored lead times can also be defined for such process chains. 
Individual processes related to process chains can also only be based on specific cause information 
reported events. The processes belonging to the chain always have a connecting factor, the same 
location ID, contract ID or customer ID and/or the associated message identifier.  
An example of such process chains is the announcement of a new sales contract in a moving situation and 
related new online contract confirmation. When the seller announces a new sales contract 
to the datahub and the datahub concludes that it is a move, it sends this to the network company 
online agreement to be confirmed. Based on this, an open system is created in the Datahub system 
event information for the network company, which becomes ready only after the network company is 
reported confirmation to datahub. The time limit for the event is two business dayseh 
from the notification received from datahub. This event appears as an open event in the network company 
in the data. These two business days have been defined as the lead time of the process chain and the data hub
the operator, like the network company itself, has the opportunity to monitor that the event is responded to 
within the time limits. Datahub's user interface has its own control view for such openings 
for events.  
Some events cannot be reported except as part of a process chain. For example 
confirmation of the online contract cannot be reported to datahub other than when the seller is 
notified datahub of a new sales contract based on which an unconfirmed one has been created 
network contract and open transaction for the distribution system operator.

is part of the process chain under certain conditions, but not always. For example, DH-312 should follow DH-311 
happens if a new network contract is needed for the place of use.

3.16 
System accessibility 
The principles related to the accessibility of the system and the support service model are included by the partyten and 
to the service agreement between datahub. However, the same are described in this document 
the principles according to which the datahub system is available to the parties and according to which 
the operator will support the industry in using the datahub system. 
Basically, the system is always available, i.e. 24/7, unless there are disturbances or the system is down 
there are no pre-planned maintenance breaks. 
The system's environment (facilities, equipment) will be of high accessibility (usability) 
environment, i.e. it is designed in such a way that the accessibility of the environment is at least level 
99.9%, i.e. outages caused by the system's environment statistically occur during the year, 
taking into account all the hours of the year, should be around 9 hours at the most. Also the system and 
with regard to the system environment's data security and data communication, there must be readiness to support high 
accessibility. 
The operation support service of the system environment is at the level of the target response times for disturbances 
and in terms of solution times, that it supports the set level of accessibility. 
These solutions aim to create the best possible conditions so that the datahub system itself 
is accessible and that it is in use and that the possible disruption is not caused by the data hub's hardware 
and environmental factors.  
The use of the system, i.e. the applications themselves that are used in the data hub, requires disruption and operation support and 
an organization ready for that, which takes care of communication between the different parties 
between user organizations and service provider organizations. Support makes sure that 
disturbances detected by users or situations related to assistance in use are resolved by the industry 
within the agreed response times. Disorders are classified according to severity levels and for everyone 
a resolution time is defined for the severity level. Disturbances can occur e.g. in the operation of applications, 
in user interfaces with which the system is used or in data exchange interfaces between different systems and 
between the datahub system. 
With regard to their systems connected to the datahub system, the parties must maintain a corresponding interference 
and user support if the fault investigation requires it, which is responsible for the party in question 
on communication and investigation regarding disturbance situations.  
3.16.1 
Users related to system administration 
Users related to system management and troubleshooting are: 
• 
data hub administrators named by distribution network operators and sellers, who correspond to the information 
from the mediation of distribution system operators and sellers' own measurement and customer information systems and 
datahub system or use directly via the user interface datahub -
system or are responsible for its functionality. Companies have an obligation to keep the information 
about the main user(s) up to date in the datahub system.

3.16.2 
System support service model 
A disturbance situation in which support service is needed can occur at any user level. It can be seen 
for the customer, e.g. so that the process used to manage the creation of a new electricity contract and electricity 
the connection to the new place of use does not go through and thus a new contract and connection cannot be obtained 
confirmed.  
The disorder can be caused by: 
• 
Datahub system not working or malfunctioning, 
• 
With the Datahub system and the datahub systems of the seller or the distribution system operator 
connections, intermediary services or applications between communicating systems 
from inaction or wrongdoing, 
• 
the system that communicates with the vendor's or distribution network operator's data hub 
from inaction or wrongdoing. 
• 
denial of service attack from an external party in terms of system use. 
Disturbance, e.g., in the delivery of data of one distribution system operator and in the event of a disruption in processes can 
affects the operation of the entire datahub system and the termination of processes.  
The system's support service model is three-tiered: 
1st step support: The customer (consumer/company) is in contact with the seller/distribution system operator 
for customer service/support in all situations concerning the customership of the end customer, 
services, invoicing, collection and contract terms with the distribution network operator/electricity seller. 
The end customer is also in contact with the distribution network operator/electricity seller in all of them 
in situations that concern the data stored in the data hub from the end customertoja This support holds 
also includes guidance on the datahub's end customer user interface. 
The end customer (consumer/company) is in contact with Fingrid Datahub's customer service 
in situations where the end customer's contact concerns the data hub's end customer 
user interface operation error situations, data security, data protection obligations or the service 
accessibility. 
2nd step support: The designated principal users/support persons of the seller/distribution system operator will contact you 
To Fingrid's datahub support service, if the problem cannot be resolved with the 1st step support.

3.16.2.1 
Reporting of disturbances 
The Datahub system has its own system for managing disturbances where the main users can 
reports the disturbances it detects. The company's main user classifies the severity of the disturbance (1-4). Fingrid's -
the main user can, if necessary, justifiably modify the severity information of the disturbance. Information about the change comes out 
to the person who reported it. In case of a disturbance, the main users are also in touch, if necessary 
by other means.  
The main users of the companies can only see and follow the progress of the problem investigation in their own company 
for reported disturbances. 
Disorder severity categories: 
1. System use is completely blocked or use of a single part classified as critical is 
completely blocked (class critical, critical). 
2. The use of the system is partially blocked and there is no workaround or a single one 
the use of the part is completely blocked (class high). 
3. A system malfunction causes significant harm to its use, but the system is 
available and a detour for use exists (disruptive category). 
4. A system malfunction causes a slight inconvenience to its use, but the system is available 
(class low, low) 
The critical functional areas of the system are:  
All the following transactions related to contract processes (DH-300): 
• 
DH-310 Creation of contracts 
• 
DH-330 Termination of Contracts 
• 
DH-340 Cancellation of Contracts 
• 
DH-350 Cancellation of contract terminations 
Events related to switching processes 
• 
DH-411 Vendor connection request

3.16.2.2 
Support on call 
The system's support on-call must be available on all stairs on weekdays from 07:00 to 19:00.  
In addition, in a critical situation, troubleshooting the 3rd stage support will continue until 10:00 p.m. This one 
after, investigation of the disturbance continues on the next weekday at 07:00.  
All three levels of the support service model must be ready to start any disruptions 
negotiation. The response time, i.e. reaction to the disturbance (taken under work) must be classified according to severity 
the next one, starting from when the malfunction has been detected and reported via the Support Service 
1. Severity category critical, response time 1 hour, solution proposal 5 hours, within service hours 
2. Severity category high, response time 2 hours, solution proposal 45 hours, within service hours 
3. Severity category disturbing, response time 1 business day, proposed solution 1 month 
4. Severity category low, response time 3 business days, solution proposal 3 months  
Severity categories 1 critical and 2 high with regard to investigating disturbances with the disturbance reported 
the main user/support person of the party must be accessible to the Datahub system 
according to the schedules of the emergency room, incl. solving critical problems on weekdays at 22:00 
until. 
After this, the investigation and eventual resolution of the problem will continue without interruption as necessary 
with the stair support staff within the aforementioned response times.  
3.16.3 
Planned maintenance outages of the system 
The planned maintenance breaks of the Datahub system will be notified to the main users of the parties no later than 3 
business day before the scheduled start time of the maintenance outage. Maintenance breaks can be done at any time 
day between 00:00 and 06:00. 
However, maintenance breaks cannot be made at the following times: 
• 
The turn of the year (23.12.-7.1.), start and end times of studies (15.8.-15.9. and 15.-
31.5.) 
• 
Change of the month: The last 3 days of the month and the first 3 days of the month 
• 
The first weekday 
• 
During the day 06-24 
The parties connected to the Datahub system must stop the transmission of data in their own systems and 
datahub system intervalwith for the duration of the maintenance break or buffer the events in your own 
in their systems.

Appendix A Descriptions of balance sheet calculations 
This appendix describes in more detail how the items to be calculated are selected for the balance sheet calculations 
time series. In the descriptions of the calculations, input refers to the information that must be provided 
to perform an individual balance sheet calculation. Other selection conditions mean those conditions, 
on the basis of which the time series used as the basis for the calculations are selected. of these terms 
fulfillment is checked in time steps and the amount selected is calculated 
from the time series only those values ​​when all conditions are met. Based on location information 
in the performed calculations, time step-specific ones can change, especially the measurement method of the place of use. 
In practice, the type of place of use cannot change, and the measurement area to which the place of use belongs changes 
very rarely. 
A.1 
Seller's measured total delivery 
Description: 
The amount calculated per seller and measurement area, for the official balance sheet period in use 
according to, from the measurement time series of the places where continuous measurement is used. 
Datahub's balance sheet type ID: BI02 
Input: 
• 
Seller 
• 
Measurement range 
Other selection criteria for measurement time series:  
• 
With the calculated time step, the seller of the input has valid balance information for the place of use 
• 
The place of use belongs to the measurement area of ​​the input 
• 
Type of place of use = Consumption 
• 
Type of measurement time series at the place of use = Active energy 
• 
Place of use measurement method = Continuous measurement 
A.2 
Seller's profiled sum delivery 
Description: 
The amount calculated per seller and measurement area, for the official balance sheet period in use 
in accordance, from the measurement time series of profiled, i.e. other than continuous measurement locations.
